**Bengaluru**,[^2] also known as **Bangalore** (its [official name](/wiki/List_of_renamed_places_in_India#Karnataka "List of renamed places in India") until 1 November 2014), is the [capital](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") and largest city of the [southern Indian](/wiki/South_India "South India") state of [Karnataka](/wiki/Karnataka "Karnataka"). As per the [2011 census](/wiki/2011_Census_of_India "2011 Census of India"), the city had a population of 8.4 million, making it the [third most populous city](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_India_by_population "List of cities in India by population") in India and the most populous in South India. The Bengaluru metropolitan area had a population of around 8.5 million, making it the [fifth most populous urban agglomeration](/wiki/List_of_million-plus_urban_agglomerations_in_India "List of million-plus urban agglomerations in India") in the country. It is located towards the southern end of the [Deccan Plateau](/wiki/Deccan_Plateau "Deccan Plateau"), at an altitude of 900 m (3,000 ft) above sea level. The city is known as India's "Garden City", due to its parks and greenery. 

Archaeological artefacts indicate that the human settlement in the region happened as early as 4000 [BCE](/wiki/Common_Era "Common Era"). The first mention of the name "Bengaluru" is from an old [Kannada](/wiki/Kannada "Kannada") stone inscription from 890 CE found at the [Nageshwara Temple](/wiki/Nageshvara_Temple,_Begur "Nageshvara Temple, Begur") in [Begur](/wiki/Begur,_Bangalore "Begur, Bangalore"). The region was ruled by the [Western Ganga dynasty](/wiki/Western_Ganga_dynasty "Western Ganga dynasty") since 350 CE, and became part of the [Chola Empire](/wiki/Chola_Empire "Chola Empire") in the early eleventh century CE. In the late [Middle Ages](/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"), it formed a part of the [Hoysala kingdom](/wiki/Hoysala_kingdom "Hoysala kingdom") and then the [Vijayanagara Empire](/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire "Vijayanagara Empire"). In 1537 CE, [Kempe Gowda I](/wiki/Kempe_Gowda_I "Kempe Gowda I"), a feudal ruler under the Vijayanagara Empire, established a [mud fort](/wiki/Bengaluru_Pete "Bengaluru Pete") which is considered the foundation of the modern city of Bengaluru with the earlier established areas (*petes*) still in existence. After the fall of the Vijayanagara Empire, Kempe Gowda declared independence, and the city was expanded by his successors. In 1638 CE, an [Adil Shahi](/wiki/Sultanate_of_Bijapur "Sultanate of Bijapur") army defeated Kempe Gowda III, and the city became a [jagir](/wiki/Jagir "Jagir") (feudal estate) of [Shahaji](/wiki/Shahaji "Shahaji"). The [Mughals](/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire") later captured the city and sold it to [Chikka Devaraja Wodeyar](/wiki/Chikka_Devaraja_Wodeyar "Chikka Devaraja Wodeyar"), the [Maharaja](/wiki/Maharaja_of_Mysore "Maharaja of Mysore") of the [Kingdom of Mysore](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore "Kingdom of Mysore"). After the death of [Krishnaraja Wodeyar II](/wiki/Krishnaraja_Wodeyar_II "Krishnaraja Wodeyar II") in 1759 CE, [Hyder Ali](/wiki/Hyder_Ali "Hyder Ali") seized control of the kingdom and with it, the administration of Bengaluru, which passed subsequently to his son, [Tipu Sultan](/wiki/Tipu_Sultan "Tipu Sultan"). 

The city was captured by the [British East India Company](/wiki/British_East_India_Company "British East India Company") during the [Anglo-Mysore Wars](/wiki/Anglo-Mysore_Wars "Anglo-Mysore Wars"), and became part of the princely state of Mysore. The administrative control of the city was returned to [Krishnaraja Wodeyar III](/wiki/Krishnaraja_Wodeyar_III "Krishnaraja Wodeyar III"), then Maharaja of Mysore, and the old city re-developed under the dominion of the Mysore kingdom. In 1809 CE, the British formed a military garrison in the city and established the [cantonment](/wiki/Bangalore_Cantonment "Bangalore Cantonment") outside the old city. In the late 19th century CE, the city was composed of two distinct urban settlements, the old Pete and the new Cantonment. Following [India's independence](/wiki/Independence_of_India "Independence of India") in 1947, Bengaluru became the capital of [Mysore State](/wiki/Mysore_State "Mysore State"), and remained the capital when the state was [enlarged and unified](/wiki/Unification_of_Karnataka "Unification of Karnataka") in 1956 and subsequently renamed as Karnataka in 1973. The two urban settlements which had developed as independent entities, merged under a single urban administration in 1949. 

Bengaluru is one of the fastest-growing metropolises in India. As of 2023, the metropolitan area had an estimated [GDP](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") of $359.9 billion, and is one of the [most productive metro areas](/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP "List of cities by GDP") of India. The city is a major centre for information technology (IT), and is consistently ranked amongst the world's fastest growing technology hubs. As the largest hub and exporter of IT services in the country, it is regarded as the "[Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley") of India". Manufacturing is a major contributor to the economy with the city home to several [state-owned units](/wiki/Public_sector_units "Public sector units"). The city also hosts several prominent institutes of higher education and of [national importance](/wiki/Institutes_of_National_Importance "Institutes of National Importance"). 

## Etymology

The earliest known reference to the name "Bengaluru" was on a ninth-century [hero stone](/wiki/Hero_stone "Hero stone") or *vīra gallu* found in [Begur](/wiki/Begur,_Bangalore "Begur, Bangalore"). The Old [Kannada](/wiki/Kannada "Kannada") inscription belonging to the [Western Ganga dynasty](/wiki/Western_Ganga_dynasty "Western Ganga dynasty") mentions the place in a battle in 890 [CE](/wiki/Common_Era "Common Era").[^14] However, [Kempe Gowda I](/wiki/Kempe_Gowda_I "Kempe Gowda I") used the name of a village near [Kodigehalli](/wiki/Kodigehalli "Kodigehalli"), to name the city as Bengaluru during its foundation in 1537 CE. Bangalore is an [anglicised](/wiki/Anglicised "Anglicised") version of the city's Kannada name. The city was also referred to as "Kalyānapura" or "Kalyānapuri" ("Auspicious City") and "Dēvarāyapattana" during the later [Vijayanagara Empire](/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire "Vijayanagara Empire") period in 16th century CE.[^15] 

An [apocryphal](/wiki/Apocryphal "Apocryphal") story states that the twelfth-century [Hoysala](/wiki/Hoysala "Hoysala") king [Veera Ballala II](/wiki/Veera_Ballala_II "Veera Ballala II"), while on a hunting expedition, lost his way in the forest. Tired and hungry, he came across a poor old woman who served him boiled beans. The grateful king named the place "Benda-Kaal-uru" (literally, "town of boiled beans"), which eventually evolved into "Bengalūru".[^15][^16] [Suryanath Kamath](/wiki/Suryanath_U._Kamath "Suryanath U. Kamath") has hypothesised that the name was derived from *benga*, the Kannada term for *[Pterocarpus marsupium](/wiki/Pterocarpus_marsupium "Pterocarpus marsupium")* (also known as the Indian Kino Tree), a species of dry and moist [deciduous trees](/wiki/Deciduous_tree "Deciduous tree") that grows abundantly in the region.[^17] Other theories include that the city was called as "Venkaturu" because of the [Venkataramana](/wiki/Venkateswara "Venkateswara") temples built by Kempe Gowda, and "Benacha kalluru" because of the abundance of [quartz](/wiki/Quartz "Quartz") stones ("benacha kal" in Kannada) in the region.[^15] 

On 11 December 2005, the [Government of Karnataka](/wiki/Government_of_Karnataka "Government of Karnataka") accepted a proposal by [U. R. Ananthamurthy](/wiki/U._R._Ananthamurthy "U. R. Ananthamurthy") to officially [rename](/wiki/Renaming_of_cities_in_India "Renaming of cities in India") the city from Bangalore to Bengaluru.[^18] On 27 September 2006, the [Bruhat Bengaluru Mahanagara Palike](/wiki/Bruhat_Bengaluru_Mahanagara_Palike "Bruhat Bengaluru Mahanagara Palike") passed a resolution to implement the name change, and the government of Karnataka officially implemented the name change from 1 November 2014 after the [Union government](/wiki/Government_of_India "Government of India") approved the request.[^19][^20][^21] 

## History

### Early and Middle Ages

[Stone Age](/wiki/Stone_Age "Stone Age") artefacts discovered at [Jalahalli](/wiki/Jalahalli "Jalahalli"), Sidhapura and Jadigenahalli on Bengaluru's outskirts indicate human settlement around 4000 BCE.[^22][^23] [Iron Age](/wiki/Iron_Age "Iron Age") tools and burial mounds from around 800 BCE, have been found in [Koramangala](/wiki/Koramangala "Koramangala") and [Chikkajala](/wiki/Chikkajala "Chikkajala"). Coins of the [Roman emperors](/wiki/Roman_emperor "Roman emperor") [Augustus](/wiki/Augustus "Augustus"), [Tiberius](/wiki/Tiberius "Tiberius"), [Claudius](/wiki/Claudius "Claudius"), and [Caligula](/wiki/Caligula "Caligula") found at [Yeswanthpur](/wiki/Yeswanthpur "Yeswanthpur") and [HAL](/wiki/HAL_Airport "HAL Airport") indicate the involvement of the region in trans-oceanic trade with the [Romans](/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome") and other civilisations in the first century CE.[^15] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Naganatheshvara_Temple_%289th_century%29_at_Begur%2C_Bengaluru.JPG/250px-Naganatheshvara_Temple_%289th_century%29_at_Begur%2C_Bengaluru.JPG)](/wiki/File:Naganatheshvara_Temple_\(9th_century\)_at_Begur,_Bengaluru.JPG)

Begur [Nageshwara Temple](/wiki/Nageshvara_Temple,_Begur "Nageshvara Temple, Begur") was built around c. 860, during the reign of the [Western Ganga dynasty](/wiki/Western_Ganga_dynasty "Western Ganga dynasty").

The region of modern-day Bengaluru was part of several successive [South Indian](/wiki/South_India "South India") kingdoms. Between the fourth and tenth centuries CE, the region was ruled by the [Western Ganga dynasty](/wiki/Western_Ganga_dynasty "Western Ganga dynasty"), the first dynasty to set up effective control over the region.[^24] According to [Edgar Thurston](/wiki/Edgar_Thurston "Edgar Thurston"), twenty-eight kings ruled Gangavadi from the start of the Common Era until its conquest by the [Cholas](/wiki/Cholas "Cholas") in the early eleventh century CE. The Western Gangas ruled as a sovereign power from 350 to 550 CE, and as feudatories of the [Chalukyas of Badami](/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty "Chalukya dynasty"), and later the [Rashtrakutas](/wiki/Rashtrakutas "Rashtrakutas") until the tenth century.[^17] The Begur [Nageshwara Temple](/wiki/Nageshvara_Temple,_Begur "Nageshvara Temple, Begur") was commissioned around 860 CE, during the reign of the Western Ganga King Ereganga Nitimarga I, and extended by his successor Nitimarga II.[^25][^26] Around 1004 CE, during the reign of [Raja Raja Chola I](/wiki/Rajaraja_I "Rajaraja I"), the Cholas defeated the Western Gangas under the command of the crown prince [Rajendra Chola I](/wiki/Rajendra_I "Rajendra I"), and captured the region.[^25][^27] During this period, the region witnessed the migration of many groups—warriors, administrators, traders, artisans, pastorals, cultivators, and religious personnel from the Southern [Tamil](/wiki/Tamil_language "Tamil language") speaking regions and other Kannada-speaking parts of the region.[^24] The Cholas built many [temples in the region](/wiki/List_of_Chola_temples_in_Bengaluru "List of Chola temples in Bengaluru") including the [Chokkanathaswamy temple](/wiki/Domlur_Chokkanathaswamy_temple "Domlur Chokkanathaswamy temple"), [Mukthi Natheshwara Temple](/wiki/Mukthi_Natheshwara_Temple "Mukthi Natheshwara Temple"), [Choleshwara Temple](/wiki/Nageshvara_Temple,_Begur "Nageshvara Temple, Begur"), and [Someshwara Temple](/wiki/Halasuru_Someshwara_Temple,_Bengaluru "Halasuru Someshwara Temple, Bengaluru").[^25] 

In 1117, the [Hoysala](/wiki/Hoysala_Kingdom "Hoysala Kingdom") king [Vishnuvardhana](/wiki/Vishnuvardhana "Vishnuvardhana") defeated the Cholas in the Battle of Talakad in south Karnataka, and extended his rule over the region.[^25][^28] In the later part of the 13th century CE, Bengaluru was a source of contention between two warring cousins, the Hoysala ruler [Veera Ballala III](/wiki/Veera_Ballala_III "Veera Ballala III") of [Halebidu](/wiki/Halebidu "Halebidu") and Ramanatha, who administered the Hoysala held territory in the southern Tamil speaking regions.[^25] Veera Ballala appointed a civic head at Hudi (suburb of the city) to administer the region, and promoted the village to the status of a town. After Veera Ballala's death in 1343, the region came under [Vijayanagara empire](/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire "Vijayanagara Empire"), which saw the rule of four consecutive dynasties – [Sangamas](/wiki/Sangama_dynasty "Sangama dynasty") (1336–1485), [Saluvas](/wiki/Saluva_dynasty "Saluva dynasty") (1485–1491), [Tuluvas](/wiki/Tuluva_dynasty "Tuluva dynasty") (1491–1565), and [Aravidu](/wiki/Aravidu_dynasty "Aravidu dynasty") (1565–1646).[^29] In the early 16th century CE, [Achyuta Deva Raya](/wiki/Achyuta_Deva_Raya "Achyuta Deva Raya") built a dam across the [Arkavati](/wiki/Arkavathi_River "Arkavathi River") river near [Hesaraghatta](/wiki/Hesaraghatta_Lake "Hesaraghatta Lake"), whose reservoir was used to supply water to the region.[^30] 

### Foundation and early modern history

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Bangalore_Fort.jpg/250px-Bangalore_Fort.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangalore_Fort.jpg)

[Bangalore Fort](/wiki/Bangalore_Fort "Bangalore Fort") in 1860 CE showing fortifications and barracks. The fort was originally built by [Kempe Gowda I](/wiki/Kempe_Gowda_I "Kempe Gowda I") as a mud fort in 1537 CE.

The city proper was established in 1537 CE by [Kempe Gowda I](/wiki/Kempe_Gowda_I "Kempe Gowda I"), a local governor and [chieftain](/wiki/Chieftain "Chieftain") aligned with the [Vijayanagara Empire](/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire "Vijayanagara Empire") under emperor [Achyuta Deva Raya](/wiki/Achyuta_Deva_Raya "Achyuta Deva Raya"). He led a campaign against Gangaraja, whom he defeated and expelled to [Kanchi](/wiki/Kanchipuram "Kanchipuram"), and built a [mud-brick fort](/wiki/Bengaluru_Pete "Bengaluru Pete") at the site, which later became the central part of the modern city of Bengaluru. Kempe Gowda referred to the new town as his "Gandubhūmi" ("Land of Heroes").[^31] Within the fort, the town was divided into smaller divisions, each called a *pētē* (Kannada pronunciation: [\[peːteː\]](/wiki/Help:IPA "Help:IPA")).[^32] The town had two main streets Chickpet and Doddapete, which intersected to form the Doddapete Square in the heart of the town.[^33] Kempe Gowda also built the temple at [Basavanagudi](/wiki/Dodda_Basavana_Gudi "Dodda Basavana Gudi"), and expanded other temples. He also constructed various tanks such as Kempambudhi, Dharmambudhi, and Sampangi for water storage.[^34] [Vijayanagara literature](/wiki/Vijayanagara_literature "Vijayanagara literature") refers to the city by various names such as "Devarāyanagara" and "Kalyānapura" or "Kalyānapuri" ("auspicious city").[^35] 

After the fall of the Vijayanagara Empire in 1565 CE in the [Battle of Talikota](/wiki/Battle_of_Talikota "Battle of Talikota"), Kempe Gowda declared independence. His successor, Kempe Gowda II, built four towers to mark the boundary of the town.[^36] In 1638 CE, a [Adil Shahi](/wiki/Sultanate_of_Bijapur "Sultanate of Bijapur") army led by [Ranadulla Khan](/wiki/Ranadulla_Khan "Ranadulla Khan") and [Shahaji Bhonsle](/wiki/Shahaji "Shahaji") (father of [Shivaji](/wiki/Shivaji "Shivaji")) defeated Kempe Gowda III, and the region became a *[jagir](/wiki/Jagir "Jagir")* (feudal estate) of Shahaji.[^34] In 1639 CE, Shahaji ordered the reconstruction of the town and built large fortifications, and new reservoirs to solve the water shortage in the region.[^34][^35] In 1687 CE, [Mughal](/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire") general Kasim Khan, under orders from [Aurangzeb](/wiki/Aurangzeb "Aurangzeb"), defeated [Ekoji I](/wiki/Ekoji_I "Ekoji I"), the son of Shahaji, and leased the town to [Chikkadevaraja Wodeyar](/wiki/Chikkadevaraja_Wodeyar "Chikkadevaraja Wodeyar") (1673–1704 CE), the then ruler of the [Kingdom of Mysore](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore "Kingdom of Mysore").[^34] After the death of [Krishnaraja Wodeyar II](/wiki/Krishnaraja_Wodeyar_II "Krishnaraja Wodeyar II") in 1759 CE, [Hyder Ali](/wiki/Hyder_Ali "Hyder Ali"), Commander-in-Chief of the Mysore Army, proclaimed himself the ruler of the Mysore kingdom. He built the Delhi and Mysore gates at the northern and southern ends of the city in 1760 CE.[^37] The kingdom later passed to Hyder Ali's son [Tipu Sultan](/wiki/Tipu_Sultan "Tipu Sultan"), and the [Lal Bagh](/wiki/Lal_Bagh "Lal Bagh") garden was established around 1760 CE.[^38] During the period, the city developed into a commercial and military centre of strategic importance.[^35] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bangalore_palace_side_view.jpg/250px-Bangalore_palace_side_view.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangalore_palace_side_view.jpg)

[Bengaluru Palace](/wiki/Bengaluru_Palace "Bengaluru Palace"), built in 1887 in [Tudor architectural style](/wiki/Tudor_architecture "Tudor architecture") was modelled on [Windsor Castle](/wiki/Windsor_Castle "Windsor Castle") in England.[^39]

The Bengaluru fort was captured by [British forces](/wiki/British_East_India_Company "British East India Company") under [Charles Cornwallis](/wiki/Charles_Cornwallis,_1st_Marquess_Cornwallis "Charles Cornwallis, 1st Marquess Cornwallis") on 21 March 1791 during the [Third Anglo-Mysore War](/wiki/Third_Anglo-Mysore_War "Third Anglo-Mysore War") and became the centre for British resistance against Tipu.[^40] Following Tipu's death in the [Fourth Anglo-Mysore War](/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Mysore_War "Fourth Anglo-Mysore War") (1799 CE), the Bengaluru Pete was incorporated into the [Princely State of Mysore](/wiki/Princely_State_of_Mysore "Princely State of Mysore"), whose administrative control remained with the [Maharaja of Mysore](/wiki/Maharaja_of_Mysore "Maharaja of Mysore"). The city was further developed by the Maharaja of Mysore. The [Residency of Mysore State](/wiki/Raj_Bhavan_\(Karnataka\) "Raj Bhavan (Karnataka)"), established in [Mysore](/wiki/Mysore "Mysore") in 1799 was shifted to Bengaluru in 1804.[^41] It was abolished in 1843 before being revived in 1881 and served till the [Indian independence](/wiki/Independence_of_India "Independence of India") in 1947.[^41][^42] The British found the city as an appropriate place to station its [garrison](/wiki/Garrison "Garrison") and therefore it was moved in 1809 from [Seringapatam](/wiki/Seringapatam "Seringapatam") to [Ulsoor](/wiki/Ulsoor "Ulsoor"), about 6 km (4 mi) northeast of the original Pete. A town grew up around the surroundings by absorbing several villages in the area, and came to be known as Bengaluru cantonment. The new centre had its own municipal and administrative apparatus, though technically it was a British enclave within the territory of the princely state of [Mysore](/wiki/Mysore "Mysore").[^43] Further developments such as the introduction of telegraph connections to other major Indian cities in 1853 and a rail connection to [Madras](/wiki/Madras "Madras") in 1864, contributed to the economic growth of the city.[^44] 

### Later modern and contemporary history

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bangalore_Pete_in_the_1890s.jpg/250px-Bangalore_Pete_in_the_1890s.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangalore_Pete_in_the_1890s.jpg)

A view of [Bengaluru Pete](/wiki/Bengaluru_Pete "Bengaluru Pete") during the 1890s

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bangalore_Cantonment.jpg/250px-Bangalore_Cantonment.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangalore_Cantonment.jpg)

A view of [Bangalore Cantonment](/wiki/Bangalore_Cantonment "Bangalore Cantonment"), c. 1895

In the late 19th century CE, Bengaluru was essentially composed of two cities, with the Pete, whose residents were predominantly [Kannadigas](/wiki/Kannadiga "Kannadiga") and the Cantonment created by the British, whose residents were predominantly [Tamils](/wiki/Tamils "Tamils") and [English people](/wiki/English_people "English people").[^45][^46] Throughout the 19th century, the Cantonment, which was known as the Civil and Military Station of Bangalore, gradually expanded and acquired a distinct cultural and political salience. It had a large military presence and a cosmopolitan civilian population that came from outside the state of Mysore.[^45] The British developed the infrastructure of the city, widened roads, and established new settlements. The city was divided into eight wards in 1862, and was expanding. The first exclusive residential area was established in [Chamarajpet](/wiki/Chamarajpet "Chamarajpet") in 1892, and a new wholesale market was established in Tharagupet in 1895.[^47] The city was hit by a [plague](/wiki/Bubonic_plague "Bubonic plague") epidemic in 1898 that claimed nearly 3,500 lives. The crisis caused by the outbreak led to the improvement in sanitation facilities, and establishment of new communication lines to co-ordinate anti-plague operations. Regulations for building new houses with proper sanitation facilities came into effect, a health officer was appointed, and the city was divided into four wards for better co-ordination.[^48][^49] New extensions in [Malleshwaram](/wiki/Malleshwaram "Malleshwaram") and [Basavanagudi](/wiki/Basavanagudi "Basavanagudi") were developed in the north and south of the Pete.[^50] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bangalore_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg/250px-Bangalore_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangalore_\(Baedeker,_1914\).jpg)

Map of the city and environs, c. 1914

In 1906, Bengaluru became one of the first cities in India to have electricity.[^51] In 1912, the [Bangalore torpedo](/wiki/Bangalore_torpedo "Bangalore torpedo"), an explosive weapon used in [World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") and [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), was devised in Bengaluru by [British army officer](/wiki/British_Indian_Army "British Indian Army") Captain McClintock of the [Madras Sappers and Miners](/wiki/Madras_Engineer_Group "Madras Engineer Group").[^52] Bengaluru's reputation as the "Garden City of India" began in 1927 with the [silver jubilee](/wiki/Silver_jubilee "Silver jubilee") celebrations of the rule of [Krishnaraja Wodeyar IV](/wiki/Krishnaraja_Wodeyar_IV "Krishnaraja Wodeyar IV"). Several projects such as the construction of parks, public buildings and hospitals were instituted to improve the city.[^53] Bengaluru played an important role during the [Indian independence movement](/wiki/Indian_independence_movement "Indian independence movement"). [Mahatma Gandhi](/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi "Mahatma Gandhi") visited the city in 1927 and 1934 and addressed public meetings here.[^22] In 1926, the [labour unrest](/wiki/1926_Binny_Mills_Strike "1926 Binny Mills Strike") in [Binny Mills](/wiki/Binny_Mills "Binny Mills") due to demand by textile workers for payment of bonus resulted in a [baton charge](/wiki/Baton_charge "Baton charge") and police firing, resulting in the death of four workers, and several injuries.[^54] In July 1928, there were notable [communal disturbances](/wiki/Bangalore_disturbances "Bangalore disturbances") in Bengaluru, like when a [Ganesh](/wiki/Ganesha "Ganesha") idol was removed from a school compound in the Sultanpet area of Bengaluru.[^55] In 1940, the first flight between Bengaluru and [Mumbai](/wiki/Mumbai "Mumbai") took off, which placed the city on India's urban map.[^56] 

After India's independence in August 1947, Bengaluru remained in the newly carved [Mysore State](/wiki/Mysore_State "Mysore State") of which the Maharaja of Mysore was the *[Rajapramukh](/wiki/Rajapramukh "Rajapramukh")* (appointed governor).[^57] The "City Improvement Trust" was formed in 1945, and in 1949, the "City" and the "Cantonment" merged to form the [Bengaluru City Corporation](/wiki/Bruhat_Bengaluru_Mahanagara_Palike "Bruhat Bengaluru Mahanagara Palike").[^58] The [Government of Karnataka](/wiki/Government_of_Karnataka "Government of Karnataka") later constituted the [Bangalore Development Authority](/wiki/Bangalore_Development_Authority "Bangalore Development Authority") in 1976 to coordinate the activities of these two bodies.[^59] Public sector employment and education provided opportunities for Kannadigas from the rest of the state to migrate to the city. Bengaluru experienced rapid growth in the decades 1941–51 and 1971–81, which saw the arrival of many immigrants from northern Karnataka. By 1961, Bengaluru had become the sixth-largest city in India, with a population of 1,207,000.[^35] In the following decades, Bengaluru's manufacturing base continued to expand with the establishment of various public and private companies.|[^60] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/UB_City_at_night_.jpg/250px-UB_City_at_night_.jpg)](/wiki/File:UB_City_at_night_.jpg)

[UB City](/wiki/UB_City "UB City"), a business district, in 2019

By the 1980s, urbanisation had spilled over the current boundaries, and in 1986, the [Bangalore Metropolitan Region Development Authority](/wiki/Bangalore_Metropolitan_Region_Development_Authority "Bangalore Metropolitan Region Development Authority"), was established to co-ordinate the development of the entire region as a single unit.[^59] On 8 February 1981, a [major fire broke out](/wiki/1981_Bangalore_circus_fire "1981 Bangalore circus fire") at Venus Circus in Bengaluru, where more than 92 people died, the majority of them children.[^61] Bengaluru experienced a growth in its real estate market in the 1980s and 1990s, spurred by capital investors from other parts of the country who converted Bengaluru's large plots and colonial [bungalows](/wiki/Bungalow "Bungalow") into multi-storied apartments.[^62] Since the late 1980s, many information technology companies were set up in the city and by the end of the 20th century, Bengaluru had established itself as the "[Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley") of India".[^35] The population has increased significantly due to migration from other parts for work, and the city has become the third most populous city in 2011.[^63][^64] During the 21st century, Bengaluru has had major terrorist attacks in [2008](/wiki/2008_Bangalore_serial_blasts "2008 Bangalore serial blasts"), [2010](/wiki/2010_Bangalore_stadium_bombing "2010 Bangalore stadium bombing"), and [2013](/wiki/2013_Bangalore_blast "2013 Bangalore blast").[^65][^66][^67] 

## Geography

Bengaluru lies in the southeast of the [South Indian](/wiki/South_India "South India") state of Karnataka in the heart of the [Mysore Plateau](/wiki/Mysore_Plateau "Mysore Plateau") (a region of the larger [Deccan Plateau](/wiki/Deccan_Plateau "Deccan Plateau")) at an average elevation of 900 m (2,953 ft).[^68][^69]: 8  The city covers an area of 741 km2 (286 sq mi).[^70] The [Bengaluru metropolitan region](/wiki/Greater_Bangalore "Greater Bangalore") covers an area of 7,005 km2 (2,705 sq mi) across three districts–[Bengaluru urban](/wiki/Bangalore_Urban_district "Bangalore Urban district"), [Bengaluru rural](/wiki/Bangalore_Rural_district "Bangalore Rural district") and [Ramanagara](/wiki/Ramanagara_District "Ramanagara District"). The [Bangalore Metropolitan Region Development Authority](/wiki/Bangalore_Metropolitan_Region_Development_Authority "Bangalore Metropolitan Region Development Authority"), established in 1985, is responsible for the planning of the metropolitan region.[^71][^72] The topography is generally flat, with the highest point at [Doddabettahalli](/wiki/Doddabettahalli "Doddabettahalli"), located 962 m (3,156 ft) above sea level on a ridge on the western part of the city. Towards the south, the terrain is uneven, with small hills and rocks made of [granite](/wiki/Granite "Granite") and [gneiss](/wiki/Gneiss "Gneiss").[^68] 

The soil in the city consist of red [laterite](/wiki/Laterite "Laterite") and red, fine [loamy](/wiki/Loam "Loam") to [clayey](/wiki/Clay "Clay") soils.[^73] The vegetation in the eastern and northern parts consists of scrubs interspersed with various water bodies, and the southern hilly region consists of scrubs and forests.[^74] The city had a forest cover of 68.3% in the early 1970s, which reduced to less than 15% in the 2010s.[^75] Trees are frequently felled to pave way for infrastructure development.[^76][^77] Though the city has been classified as a part of the seismic zone II (a stable zone), it has experienced [earthquakes](/wiki/Earthquake "Earthquake") of magnitude as high as 4.5 on the [Richter scale](/wiki/Richter_scale "Richter scale").[^78] 

### Hydrography

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/BangaloreLake.jpg/250px-BangaloreLake.jpg)](/wiki/File:BangaloreLake.jpg)

[Hesaraghatta Lake](/wiki/Hesaraghatta_Lake "Hesaraghatta Lake") in north Bengaluru

There are no major rivers run in the city, though six rivers arise at the [Nandi Hills](/wiki/Nandi_Hills,_India "Nandi Hills, India"), about 60 km (37 mi) to the north.[^68][^79] The [Vrishabhavathi](/wiki/River_Vrishabhavathi "River Vrishabhavathi"), a tributary of [Arkavathi](/wiki/Arkavathy_River "Arkavathy River") flows through the city. Arkavathi, [Dakshina Pinakini](/wiki/Dakshina_Pinakini "Dakshina Pinakini") and its tributary Chinnar, and Suvarnamukhi rivers water the fringes of the city.[^68][^80] Most of these rivers are polluted, and depleted due to sewage from the city.[^81][^82] [Kaveri](/wiki/Kaveri "Kaveri") runs towards the southwest of the city, the water from which is used to cater to majority of the water requirements of the city.[^83] The city has a considerable number of freshwater lakes and [water tanks](/wiki/Water_tank "Water tank"), most of which are seasonal and rain-fed.[^68] The city had 265 lakes in the 1960s, which shrunk to 98 by the late 2010s, and most of the city's lakes are polluted.[^74][^84][^85][^86] The government began revival and conservation efforts in 2020.[^87] Groundwater occurs in [silty](/wiki/Silt "Silt") to [sandy](/wiki/Sand "Sand") layers of the [alluvial](/wiki/Alluvial "Alluvial") sediments, and are extracted through open wells.[^68] 

### Climate

Bengaluru has a [tropical savanna climate](/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate "Tropical savanna climate") ([Köppen climate classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") *Aw*) with distinct [wet](/wiki/Wet_season "Wet season") and [dry](/wiki/Dry_season "Dry season") seasons. Due to its high elevation, Bengaluru usually enjoys a more moderate climate throughout the year, although occasional [heat waves](/wiki/Heat_wave "Heat wave") can make summer somewhat uncomfortable.[^88] The dry season extends from December to February followed by the summer season from March to May. The [monsoon](/wiki/Monsoon "Monsoon") brings most of the rainfall from June to September, followed by a post-monsoon season in October and November.[^68] April is the hottest month with an average high of 34.1 °C (93.4 °F), and January is the coolest month with an average low temperature of 15.1 °C (59.2 °F).[^89] The highest temperature ever recorded in Bengaluru was 39.2 °C (103 °F), recorded 24 April 2016, corresponding with [the strong El Niño](/wiki/2014%E2%80%932016_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event "2014–2016 El Niño event") in that year.[^90] The lowest ever recorded is 7.8 °C (46 °F) in January 1884.[^91][^92] Winter temperatures rarely drop below 14 °C (57 °F), and summer temperatures seldom exceed 36 °C (97 °F).[^68] Bengaluru receives rainfall from both the northeast and the southwest [monsoons](/wiki/Monsoon "Monsoon"), and the wettest months is September, followed by October and August.[^89] The summer heat is moderated by fairly frequent [thunderstorms](/wiki/Thunderstorm "Thunderstorm"), which occasionally cause power outages and local flooding, such as in 2022.[^93][^94][^95] Most of the rainfall occurs during the late afternoon or evening and rain before noon is infrequent.[^96] The heaviest rainfall recorded in a 24-hour period is 179 mm (7 in) recorded on 1 October 1997.[^97]

## Demographics

Population growth
| Year                                                                          | Pop.   | ±% |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------ | -- |
| 406,760                                                                       | —      |    |
| 778,977                                                                       | +91.5% |    |

| 1,654,000                                                                     | +37.0% |    |
