| Source: [Census of India](/wiki/Census_of_India "Census of India")[^63][^106] |        |    |

As per the [2011 census](/wiki/2011_census_of_India "2011 census of India"), Bengaluru had a population of 8,443,675, which made it the third [most populous city](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_India_by_population "List of cities in India by population") in India, and the largest in [South India](/wiki/South_India "South India").[^63] The urban agglomeration was home to 8,499,399 people, and was the [fifth most populous urban agglomeration](/wiki/List_of_million-plus_urban_agglomerations_in_India "List of million-plus urban agglomerations in India") in India.[^9][^107] As per a 2016 estimate, the urban agglomeration had a population of about 10.45 million.[^108] The city was amongst the fastest growing cities in the last two decades, with the population increasing substantially due to migration from rest of the country.[^63][^109] About 13.2% of the population belonged to [scheduled castes](/wiki/Scheduled_castes "Scheduled castes"), and [scheduled tribes](/wiki/Scheduled_tribes "Scheduled tribes").[^110] Residents of Bengaluru are referred to as *Bengaloorinavaru* in [Kannada](/wiki/Kannada "Kannada")[^111][^112] and "Bangaloreans" in [English](/wiki/English_language "English language").[^113] 

There are about 597 slums in the city, housing roughly 16% of the city's population.[^114][^115] The city had a [gini](/wiki/Gini_coefficient "Gini coefficient") index of 0.64, indicating significant [inequality](/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality").[^110][^116] Various studies have also indicated various inequalities in the infrastructure development across different parts of the city, and other urbanisation problems such as mass displacements, proliferation of slums, and public health crisis due to water shortage and sewage problems in poor and working-class neighbourhoods.[^117] In the *Ease of Living Index 2020* published by the [Ministry of Housing & Urban Affairs](/wiki/Ministry_of_Housing_and_Urban_Affairs "Ministry of Housing and Urban Affairs"), the city was ranked the most livable Indian city with a population of over a million.[^118] In the 2023 Quality of Living survey by [Mercer](/wiki/Mercer_\(consulting_firm\) "Mercer (consulting firm)"), which evaluated living conditions for expatriates, Bengaluru was ranked 156th globally and third in India, after [Hyderabad](/wiki/Hyderabad "Hyderabad") and [Pune](/wiki/Pune "Pune").[^119] 

### Ethnicity and religion

Religion in Bengaluru (2011)[^120]
| Religion                                          | Percent |
| ------------------------------------------------- | ------- |
| [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism")             |         |
| [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam")                      |         |
| [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") |         |
| [Jainism](/wiki/Jainism "Jainism")                |         |
| [Sikhism](/wiki/Sikhism "Sikhism")                |         |
| [Buddhism](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism")             |         |
| Others                                            |         |

According to the 2011 census, [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism") is the major religion with 78.9% of adherents. [Muslims](/wiki/Muslim "Muslim") comprisd 13.9% of the population, with [Christians](/wiki/Christians "Christians") and [Jains](/wiki/Jain "Jain") accounting for 5.6% and 1.0% of the population, respectively.[^120] Muslims in the city consist of [Dakhini](/wiki/Dakhini "Dakhini") and Urdu-speaking Muslims, [Kutchi Memons](/wiki/Kutchi_Memon "Kutchi Memon"), [Labbay](/wiki/Labbay "Labbay"), and [Mappilas](/wiki/Malabar_Muslims "Malabar Muslims").[^121] Christians in Bengaluru include [Roman Catholics](/wiki/Roman_Catholics "Roman Catholics") including [Tamil Christians](/wiki/Tamil_Christians "Tamil Christians"), [Mangalorean Catholics](/wiki/Mangalorean_Catholics "Mangalorean Catholics"), Kannadiga Christians, [Malayali Syrian Christians](/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Christians "Saint Thomas Christians"), [Protestants](/wiki/Protestants "Protestants"), and [Northeast Indian Christians](/wiki/List_of_Christian_denominations_in_Northeast_India "List of Christian denominations in Northeast India").[^122][^123][^124] 

Apart from the [Kannadigas](/wiki/Kannadigas "Kannadigas") native to the region, [Tamils](/wiki/Tamils "Tamils"), [Telugus](/wiki/Telugus "Telugus") and [Deccanis](/wiki/Deccani_people "Deccani people"), form a significant population of the city.[^125][^126][^127] In the 16th century, Tamil speakers, who also spoke Kannada, settled in the region for business.[^128] Telugus came to the city on invitation of the Mysore royalty.[^129] Since the late 20th century, there has been a steady migration of people from other states for study and work.[^130] About 90% of the migrants came from the South Indian states, with the number of migrants from other parts of India increasing over the last few decades of the 20th century. Majority of the migration from non-South Indians states included [Maharashtrians](/wiki/Maharashtrians "Maharashtrians"), [Punjabis](/wiki/Punjabis "Punjabis"), [Rajasthanis](/wiki/Rajasthanis "Rajasthanis"), [Gujaratis](/wiki/Gujaratis "Gujaratis"), [Bengalis](/wiki/Bengalis "Bengalis"), and from [Uttar Pradesh](/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh "Uttar Pradesh").[^64] Migrant communities from within the state include [Tuluvas](/wiki/Tuluvas "Tuluvas") and [Konkanis](/wiki/Konkanis "Konkanis") of coastal Karnataka, and [Kodavas](/wiki/Kodavas "Kodavas") from the state's [Kodagu district](/wiki/Kodagu_district "Kodagu district").[^125] The city also had an [Anglo-Indian](/wiki/Anglo-Indian "Anglo-Indian") population of about 10,000 people in 2006.[^131] 

### Languages

Pop. by mother tongue in Bengaluru (2011)[^132]
| Language                                          | Percent |
| ------------------------------------------------- | ------- |
| [Kannada](/wiki/Kannada "Kannada")                |         |
| [Tamil](/wiki/Tamil_language "Tamil language")    |         |
| [Telugu](/wiki/Telugu_language "Telugu language") |         |
| [Urdu](/wiki/Urdu "Urdu")                         |         |
| [Hindi](/wiki/Hindi "Hindi")                      |         |
| Others                                            |         |

As per the 2011 census, Kannada is the mother tongue of 42.1% of the city's population with 3,574,226 speakers, which is the official language of the state[^133] – followed by [Tamil](/wiki/Tamil_language "Tamil language") (1,388,305) [Telugu](/wiki/Telugu_language "Telugu language") (1,166,338), [Urdu](/wiki/Urdu "Urdu") (1,104,124), [Hindi](/wiki/Hindi "Hindi") (476,673), [Malayalam](/wiki/Malayalam "Malayalam") (268,780), and [Marathi](/wiki/Marathi_language "Marathi language") (174,451). Other languages with a sizeable numbers of speakers include [Konkani](/wiki/Konkani_language "Konkani language"), [Bengali](/wiki/Bengali_language "Bengali language"), [Marwari](/wiki/Marwari_language "Marwari language"), [Tulu](/wiki/Tulu_language "Tulu language"), [Odia](/wiki/Odia_language "Odia language"), [Gujarati](/wiki/Gujarati_language "Gujarati language"), [Kodagu](/wiki/Kodava_language "Kodava language"), [Punjabi](/wiki/Punjabi_language "Punjabi language"), [Lambadi](/wiki/Lambadi "Lambadi"), [Sindhi](/wiki/Sindhi_language "Sindhi language") and [Nepali](/wiki/Nepali_language "Nepali language").[^132] [Bengaluru Kannada](/wiki/Bengaluru_Kannada "Bengaluru Kannada") is the local dialect of Kannada spoken in the region.[^134][^135] [English](/wiki/English_language "English language") is widely spoken by [white-collar workers](/wiki/White-collar_workers "White-collar workers") and is the principal business language.[^133][^136] With a diverse population speaking multiple languages, the city has often seen [controversies](/wiki/Nativism_in_Karnataka "Nativism in Karnataka") and issues with respect to the usage of English and other vernacular languages. In 2023, the government mandated the usage of Kannada in the sign boards of all businesses, which led to protests.[^137][^138] There have also been court cases, protests, and diverse public opinion on the usage of different languages in the city.[^139][^140] 

## Administration and politics

### Administration

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/The_Municipal_Offices_Building%2C_Bangalore.jpg/250px-The_Municipal_Offices_Building%2C_Bangalore.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Municipal_Offices_Building,_Bangalore.jpg)

The Municipal office building, the seat of [Greater Bengaluru Authority](/wiki/Greater_Bengaluru_Authority "Greater Bengaluru Authority"), in the early 20th century

[Greater Bengaluru Authority](/wiki/Greater_Bengaluru_Authority "Greater Bengaluru Authority") (GBA) is the administrative authority of the city and its suburbs, covering an area of 1,400 km2 (540 sq mi).[^141][^142] The Bangalore Municipal Board was established on 27 March 1862, with a separate board formed later to manage the cantonment area of the city. In 1881, these were organised into Bangalore city municipality and Bangalore civil and military station municipality respectively. The two municipalities were merged in 1949, into a single municipal corporation with 70 members. In 2007, BBMP was established by merging the [Bangalore Mahanagara Palike](/wiki/Bangalore_Mahanagara_Palike "Bangalore Mahanagara Palike"), with seven neighbouring city municipal councils, one town municipal council and 111 village panchayats around the city.[^143] 

The GBA was established in May 2025, replacing the BBMP.[^141] The erstwhile Bengaluru corporation covered an area 741 km2 (286 sq mi), divided into ten zones covering [223 wards](/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Bengaluru "Administrative divisions of Bengaluru").[^144] The BBMP was headed by a [mayor](/wiki/Mayor "Mayor"), elected by the [councillors](/wiki/Councillors "Councillors"), who were elected through a [popular vote](/wiki/Direct_election "Direct election") by the residents.[^143][^145] The municipal commissioner was responsible for daily administration.[^146] The former BBMP was divided into five smaller city corporations.[^147] As the last elections to the BBMP council were held in 2015, and its term ended in 2020, after which the body was managed by a state-appointed administrator until the new structure was implemented.[^148] As per the [Ministry of Housing and Urban Affairs](/wiki/Ministry_of_Housing_and_Urban_Affairs "Ministry of Housing and Urban Affairs"), the BBMP had a revenue of ₹55.87 billion (US$660 million) and an expenditure of ₹64.65 billion (US$760 million) in 2021–22.[^149] 

The [Bangalore Development Authority](/wiki/Bangalore_Development_Authority "Bangalore Development Authority") (BDA) was established in 1976, and is the nodal agency responsible for the planning and development of the city.[^150] The BDA works in conjunction with local government and the Agenda for Bangalore's Infrastructure and Development Task Force (ABIDe) to design and implement civic and infrastructural projects in the city.[^143][^151] The [Bangalore Metropolitan Region Development Authority](/wiki/Bangalore_Metropolitan_Region_Development_Authority "Bangalore Metropolitan Region Development Authority"), established in 1985, is responsible for the planning of the metropolitan region.[^152] As the capital of the state of Karntaka, the city houses the state executive and [legislative](/wiki/Legislature "Legislature") headquarters in the [Vidhana Soudha](/wiki/Vidhana_Soudha "Vidhana Soudha"),[^153] state ministries at [Vikasa Soudha](/wiki/Vikasa_Soudha "Vikasa Soudha"),[^154][^155] and the residence of the [Governor](/wiki/Governor_of_Karnataka "Governor of Karnataka") at [Raj Bhavan](/wiki/Raj_Bhavan,_Karnataka "Raj Bhavan, Karnataka").[^156] 

### Law and order

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/High_Court_of_Karnataka%2C_Bangalore_MMK.jpg/250px-High_Court_of_Karnataka%2C_Bangalore_MMK.jpg)](/wiki/File:High_Court_of_Karnataka,_Bangalore_MMK.jpg)

[Karnataka High Court](/wiki/Karnataka_High_Court "Karnataka High Court") in Bengaluru is the highest judicial body in the state

[Karnataka High Court](/wiki/Karnataka_High_Court "Karnataka High Court") in Bengaluru is the highest [judicial](/wiki/Judicial "Judicial") authority in the state, and manages a series of sub-ordinate civil and criminal courts.[^157][^158] The [Bengaluru City Police](/wiki/Bengaluru_City_Police "Bengaluru City Police") (BCP) is the primary law enforcement agency in the city and is headed by a [commissioner of police](/wiki/Police_Commissioner_of_Bangalore "Police Commissioner of Bangalore").[^159] The city is divided into eight zones, each of which is headed by an [assistant commissioner](/wiki/Assistant_commissioner_\(police\) "Assistant commissioner (police)").[^160] There are separate crime, intelligence, and administration wings of the police.[^161] The police also operate special and armed units.[^162] As of February 2024, the city police consisted of 18,308 civilian police working across 113 police stations, and 6,999 armed reserve personnel. The city had 191 cops per hundred thousand people, well below the [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") standard of 673.[^163] [Bengaluru City Traffic Police](/wiki/Bengaluru_City_Traffic_Police "Bengaluru City Traffic Police") (BCTP) is responsible for the traffic management in the city.[^164] The traffic police operates 48 stations across three zones, each of which is headed by a joint commissioner.[^161][^165] As of 2021, the crime rate in the city was 27.2 per hundred thousand people.[^166] The [Bangalore Central Prison](/wiki/Bangalore_Central_Prison "Bangalore Central Prison") located at Parappana Agrahara, was established in 1997, and is the major prison in the city.[^167][^168] 

### Politics

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Vikasa_Souda_-_June_2019.jpg/250px-Vikasa_Souda_-_June_2019.jpg)](/wiki/File:Vikasa_Souda_-_June_2019.jpg)

The [Vikasa Soudha](/wiki/Vikasa_Soudha "Vikasa Soudha") houses multiple state ministries

The major part of the city falls under four [parliamentary](/wiki/Parliament_of_India "Parliament of India") constituencies–[Bangalore Rural](/wiki/Bangalore_Rural_\(Lok_Sabha_constituency\) "Bangalore Rural (Lok Sabha constituency)"), [Bangalore Central](/wiki/Bangalore_Central_\(Lok_Sabha_constituency\) "Bangalore Central (Lok Sabha constituency)"), [Bangalore North](/wiki/Bangalore_North_\(Lok_Sabha_constituency\) "Bangalore North (Lok Sabha constituency)"), and [Bangalore South](/wiki/Bangalore_South_\(Lok_Sabha_constituency\) "Bangalore South (Lok Sabha constituency)").[^169] The city elects 28 [MLAs](/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly_\(India\) "Member of the Legislative Assembly (India)") to the [Karnataka Legislative Assembly](/wiki/Karnataka_Legislative_Assembly "Karnataka Legislative Assembly").[^170] The politics of the city and the state have been dominated by the two national parties–[Indian National Congress](/wiki/Indian_National_Congress "Indian National Congress"), and [Bharatiya Janata Party](/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party "Bharatiya Janata Party") (BJP). Contrary to other major South Indian cities, there are no major regional parties with a considerable influence in the region, with only [Janata Dal (Secular)](/wiki/Janata_Dal_\(Secular\) "Janata Dal (Secular)") (JDS) having some influence.[^171] In the [2023 Karnataka Legislative Assembly election](/wiki/2023_Karnataka_Legislative_Assembly_election "2023 Karnataka Legislative Assembly election"), the BJP won 15 seats, and the Congress won 13 seats in the city.[^172] In the [2024 Indian general elections](/wiki/2024_Indian_general_elections "2024 Indian general elections"), the BJP won all the four [Lok Sabha](/wiki/Lok_Sabha "Lok Sabha") seats in the city.[^173] The last elections to the BBMP was held in [2015](/wiki/2015_Bruhat_Bengaluru_Mahanagara_Palike_election "2015 Bruhat Bengaluru Mahanagara Palike election"), in which the BJP won 100 seats, and the Congress won 76 seats. The Congress held the mayor post with the support of the JDS till 2019, after which the BJP captured power when the JDS switched its allegiance.[^174][^175] In 2020, the term of the council ended, and with no elections had since been conducted till 2024, the BBMP is managed by a government appointed administrator.[^176][^177] 

## Culture

### Arts

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Demon_Yakshagana.jpg/250px-Demon_Yakshagana.jpg)](/wiki/File:Demon_Yakshagana.jpg)

[Yakshagana](/wiki/Yakshagana "Yakshagana"), a theatre art of [coastal Karnataka](/wiki/Coastal_Karnataka "Coastal Karnataka"), played in the city

Bengaluru is a major centre of [Indian classical music](/wiki/Indian_classical_music "Indian classical music") and dance.[^178] The cultural scene features a diverse set of music concerts, dance performances and plays. Performances of [Carnatic](/wiki/Carnatic_music "Carnatic music") and [Hindustani](/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music "Hindustani classical music") music, and dance forms like [Bharat Natyam](/wiki/Bharat_Natyam "Bharat Natyam"), [Kuchipudi](/wiki/Kuchipudi "Kuchipudi"), [Kathakali](/wiki/Kathakali "Kathakali"), [Kathak](/wiki/Kathak "Kathak"), and [Odissi](/wiki/Odissi "Odissi") are popular in the city.[^179] [Yakshagana](/wiki/Yakshagana "Yakshagana"), a theatre art indigenous to coastal Karnataka is often played in town halls.[^180] The two main music seasons include April–May during [Ram Navami](/wiki/Rama_Navami "Rama Navami"), and September–October during [Dusshera](/wiki/Dusshera "Dusshera"), when majority of the music activities are organised by various cultural organisations.[^179] Rock music is popular in the urban parts of the city, and the city has its own subgenre of rock, "Bangalore Rock", an amalgamation of [classic rock](/wiki/Classic_rock "Classic rock"), [hard rock](/wiki/Hard_rock "Hard rock") and [heavy metal](/wiki/Heavy_metal_music "Heavy metal music"), and some [jazz](/wiki/Jazz "Jazz") and [blues](/wiki/Blues "Blues").[^181] The city is home to several Indian bands, and is referred to as "[Pub](/wiki/Public_house "Public house") Capital of India" and the "Rock/Metal Capital of India" because of its underground music scene.[^182] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/National_Gallery_of_Modern_Art_-_NGMA_-_Bangalore_6643.JPG/250px-National_Gallery_of_Modern_Art_-_NGMA_-_Bangalore_6643.JPG)](/wiki/File:National_Gallery_of_Modern_Art_-_NGMA_-_Bangalore_6643.JPG)

[National Gallery of Modern Art](/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Modern_Art,_Bangalore "National Gallery of Modern Art, Bangalore") in Bengaluru

Several art galleries including the government-established [National Gallery of Modern Art](/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Modern_Art,_Bangalore "National Gallery of Modern Art, Bangalore") emerged in the 1990s.[^183] The [Karnataka Chitrakala Parishath](/wiki/Karnataka_Chitrakala_Parishath "Karnataka Chitrakala Parishath") showcases a collection of painting, sculptures, and various other forms of art.[^184][^185] The Indian Cartoon Gallery organised by the [Indian Institute of Cartoonists](/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Cartoonists "Indian Institute of Cartoonists"), conducts periodic cartoon exhibitions.[^186] "Art Bangalore" is an international [art festival](/wiki/Art_festival "Art festival"), held annually in the city since 2010.[^187] [Kannada Sahitya Parishat](/wiki/Kannada_Sahitya_Parishat "Kannada Sahitya Parishat") is a nonprofit organisation headquartered in Bengaluru that promotes the Kannada language and literature.[^188] The "Bangalore Literature Festival" is an annual literary event organised since 2012.[^189] [Karnataka Rajyotsava](/wiki/Karnataka_Rajyotsava "Karnataka Rajyotsava"), which marks the formation of [Karnataka](/wiki/Karnataka "Karnataka") state on 1 November 1956, is celebrated on the same day annually and is a public holiday in the city.[^190][^191] Bengaluru is a major centre of the [Kannada film industry](/wiki/Kannada_film_industry "Kannada film industry"), which released 224 Kannada feature films in 2018.[^192] Art theatres that stages English and Kannada language plays in the city include [Chowdiah Memorial Hall](/wiki/Chowdiah_Memorial_Hall "Chowdiah Memorial Hall"), [Ranga Shankara](/wiki/Ranga_Shankara "Ranga Shankara"), and [Ravindra Kalakshetra](/wiki/Ravindra_Kalakshetra "Ravindra Kalakshetra").[^193][^194] [British Council](/wiki/British_Council "British Council"), Alliance Française de Bangalore, and Max Müller Bhavan also organise foreign language plays including those of drama companies that tour India.[^195][^196] 

### Cuisine

Bengaluru has diverse food options including South Indian, North Indian, [Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_food "Chinese food"), and western fast food.[^197][^198] Popular vegetarian dishes include [masala dosa](/wiki/Masala_dosa "Masala dosa"), paneer biryani, and [paneer butter masala](/wiki/Paneer_butter_masala "Paneer butter masala").[^199] [Udupi cuisine](/wiki/Udupi_cuisine "Udupi cuisine") restaurants are popular and serve predominantly [vegetarian](/wiki/Vegetarian "Vegetarian"), regional cuisine.[^200] [Mavalli Tiffin Room](/wiki/Mavalli_Tiffin_Room "Mavalli Tiffin Room"), known for its Karnataka-style vegetarian food, was opened in 1924 and vegetarian tiffin restaurant [Vidyarthi Bhavan](/wiki/Vidyarthi_Bhavan "Vidyarthi Bhavan") opened in 1943.[^201][^202] Since the late 1980s, many vegetarian self-service [darshinis](/wiki/Darshini_\(restaurant\) "Darshini (restaurant)") operate in the city.[^201] The city also has multiple [vegan](/wiki/Vegan "Vegan") restaurants, and vegan advocacy groups, and has been named as India's most vegan-friendly city by [PETA](/wiki/PETA "PETA") India.[^203][^204] 

### Festivals

[Bangalore Karaga](/wiki/Bangalore_Karaga "Bangalore Karaga") or "Karaga Shaktyotsava" is a festival dedicated to the Hindu goddess [Draupadi](/wiki/Draupadi "Draupadi"), and celebrated annually by the [Thigala](/wiki/Thigala "Thigala") community over a period of nine days in March or April.[^205][^206] The Someshwara Car festival is held annually in April, when the idol of the [Halasuru Someshwara Temple](/wiki/Halasuru_Someshwara_Temple,_Bangalore "Halasuru Someshwara Temple, Bangalore") is taken for a procession on a flower chariot.[^207] Other [popular festivals](/wiki/List_of_festivals_in_India "List of festivals in India") include [Ugadi](/wiki/Ugadi "Ugadi"), [Ram Navami](/wiki/Ram_Navami "Ram Navami"), [Eid ul-Fitr](/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr "Eid ul-Fitr"), [Ganesh Chaturthi](/wiki/Ganesh_Chaturthi "Ganesh Chaturthi"), [St. Mary's feast](/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Bangalore "St. Mary's Basilica, Bangalore"), [Dasara](/wiki/Navrati "Navrati"), [Deepawali](/wiki/Deepawali "Deepawali") and [Christmas](/wiki/Christmas "Christmas").[^208] 

## Economy

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/UB_Tower_Bangalore.jpg/250px-UB_Tower_Bangalore.jpg)](/wiki/File:UB_Tower_Bangalore.jpg)

[UB Tower](/wiki/UB_City "UB City") in the [Bengaluru Central Business District](/wiki/Bengaluru_Central_Business_District "Bengaluru Central Business District")

Bengaluru is one of the fastest-growing metropolises in India.[^209][^210][^211] As of 2023, Bengaluru metropolitan area had an estimated [GDP](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") of $359.9 billion,[^11] ranking it among the [most productive metro areas](/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP "List of cities by GDP") in India.[^212][^213] According to the [Globalization and World Cities Research Network](/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network "Globalization and World Cities Research Network"), Bengaluru is amongst the most integrated with the global economy, classified as an [alpha-city](/wiki/Global_city "Global city").[^214] The city contributes to nearly one-third of the state GSDP, and has a diversified industrial base dependent on [services](/wiki/Service_economy "Service economy") (39.5% contribution to GDP), manufacturing (36%), and [agriculture](/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture") (2.3%).[^215][^216] Bengaluru has the country's fourth largest [fast-moving consumer goods](/wiki/Fast-moving_consumer_goods "Fast-moving consumer goods") market.[^217] The city also has the third highest number of [high-net-worth individuals](/wiki/High-net-worth_individual "High-net-worth individual") in India.[^218] Major industrial sectors include [information technology](/wiki/Information_technology "Information technology"), [automobiles](/wiki/Automobiles "Automobiles"), [aerospace](/wiki/Aerospace "Aerospace"), [textiles](/wiki/Textiles "Textiles"), [heavy machinery](/wiki/Heavy_machinery "Heavy machinery"), [biotechnology](/wiki/Biotechnology "Biotechnology"), [electronics](/wiki/Electronics "Electronics"), and [communication](/wiki/Communication "Communication"), [agriculture](/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture"), and [food processing](/wiki/Food_processing "Food processing").[^219] The industrial clusters are spread across the city and its suburbs.[^220][^221] As of 2016, the city had more than 75,000 industries including more than 2,000 information technology companies.[^216] It hosted 87 [Fortune 500](/wiki/Fortune_500 "Fortune 500") companies, the fifth highest number amongst the cities in India.[^222] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/World_Trade_Center_Banglore_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-World_Trade_Center_Banglore_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:World_Trade_Center_Banglore_\(cropped\).jpg)

[World Trade Center](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Bangalore "World Trade Center Bangalore") at Bengaluru

Bengaluru is a major centre for information technology (IT), and is consistently ranked amongst the world's fastest growing technology hubs. [^223][^224] It is widely regarded as the "[Silicon Valley](/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley") of India", as the largest IT hub of the country.[^225][^226][^227] The IT export from the city is estimated to be valued at $64 billion in 2024, and the city contributes to more than one third of India's total IT exports.[^228][^229] The IT industry in the city is divided into various business clusters and [special economic zones](/wiki/Special_economic_zones "Special economic zones") such as [Electronic City](/wiki/Electronic_City "Electronic City"), [International Tech Park](/wiki/International_Tech_Park,_Bangalore "International Tech Park, Bangalore"), [Software Technology Park](/wiki/Software_Technology_Parks_of_India "Software Technology Parks of India"), [Bagmane Tech Park](/wiki/Bagmane_Tech_Park "Bagmane Tech Park"), [Global Village Tech Park](/wiki/Global_Village_Tech_Park "Global Village Tech Park"), [World Trade Center](/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Bangalore "World Trade Center Bangalore"), and [Manyata Embassy Business Park](/wiki/Manyata_Embassy_Business_Park "Manyata Embassy Business Park") amongst others.[^230] The growth of IT industry has resulted in the migration of people from all over the country, which has resulted in the demand for improvement in the city's infrastructure and presented the city with other challenges.[^223][^231] The industry has been blamed for not favouring local employment development, increased land values, and closure of small enterprises.[^232] The resistance from the city for further investments required to develop infrastructure, has forced some of the new and expanding businesses elsewhere.[^233] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Vande_Bharat_sleeper_trainset_prototype_at_BEML.jpeg/250px-Vande_Bharat_sleeper_trainset_prototype_at_BEML.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Vande_Bharat_sleeper_trainset_prototype_at_BEML.jpeg)

A train set manufactured at [BEML](/wiki/BEML "BEML")

Bengaluru is also a major hub for Indian biotechnology-related industry, which was valued at nearly $25 billion in 2021–22.[^234][^235] The city is home to more than 40 biotech companies, and is termed as the "Biotech capital of India".[^236][^237] The city is a major export centre for agricultural produce including [fruits](/wiki/Fruits "Fruits"), and [poultry](/wiki/Poultry "Poultry").[^238] Major crops include [rice](/wiki/Rice "Rice"), [maize](/wiki/Maize "Maize"), [ragi](/wiki/Finger_millet "Finger millet"), [horse gram](/wiki/Horse_gram "Horse gram"), [oil seeds](/wiki/Oil_seeds "Oil seeds"), [coconuts](/wiki/Coconuts "Coconuts"), and fruits such as [mango](/wiki/Mango "Mango"), [papaya](/wiki/Papaya "Papaya"), [banana](/wiki/Banana "Banana"), [grapes](/wiki/Grapes "Grapes"), and [pomegranate](/wiki/Pomegranate "Pomegranate"). Flowers such as [roses](/wiki/Roses "Roses") are grown commercially.[^216] The [Rail Wheel Factory](/wiki/Rail_Wheel_Factory "Rail Wheel Factory") at Yelahanka is a major supplier of wheels and axles for [Indian Railways](/wiki/Indian_Railways "Indian Railways").[^239] State owned corporations [BEML](/wiki/BEML "BEML") and [Bharat Electronics](/wiki/Bharat_Electronics "Bharat Electronics") are headquartered in the city, and manufacture aerospace components, power equipment, trainsets, armored vehicles, and electronics for both civilian and defence requirements.[^216][^240] 

## Infrastructure

### Water supply

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Cauvery_Kaveri_River_Karnataka_India_%282%29.jpg/250px-Cauvery_Kaveri_River_Karnataka_India_%282%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cauvery_Kaveri_River_Karnataka_India_\(2\).jpg)

The city draws majority of the water requirement from the [Kaveri River](/wiki/Kaveri_River "Kaveri River")

[Water supply](/wiki/Water_supply "Water supply") is provided by the [Bangalore Water Supply and Sewerage Board](/wiki/Bangalore_Water_Supply_and_Sewerage_Board "Bangalore Water Supply and Sewerage Board") (BWSSB), which was established in 1964.[^241] The city receives an average of 800 million liters of water per day from rainfall.[^242] In the 16th century, Kempe Gowda constructed lakes such as the Kempambudhi Kere to store the rain water.[^243] As of 2021, the city had a daily water demand of 2100 million liters, of which 1,450 million liters is catered to by the corporation. While the city drew water from the [Arkavathy River](/wiki/Arkavathy_River "Arkavathy River") earlier, the increasing demands led to the establishment of the Cauvery water supply scheme in 1964. Majority of the water supply to the city is drawn from the [Kaveri](/wiki/Kaveri "Kaveri"), with the amount of water drawn increasing from 135 million liters in 1974 to 1,450 million liters per day in 2014.[^244] A 2015 report indicated that one-third of the [slum clearance](/wiki/Slum_clearance_in_India "Slum clearance in India") projects lacked basic water service connections, 60% of slum dwellers lacked complete water supply lines and used a shared water supply.[^245] The city does face water shortages, especially during summer and in years with low rainfall.[^246] 

In early 2024, Bengaluru faced a water crisis due to depleted water reservoirs in the Kaveri basin as a consequence of a weak monsoon, and low groundwater levels.[^247] Borewells, which contribute a sufficient share to the city's water consumption, ran dry, and the government was forced to operate water tankers from outside the city and impose restrictions on non-essential water usage.[^248] 

### Waste management and pollution

Waste collection and management is done by the city corporation. Pollution regulation and issuance of waste management guidelines is carried out by the [Karnataka State Pollution Control Board](/wiki/Karnataka_State_Pollution_Control_Board "Karnataka State Pollution Control Board") (KSPCB), which comes under the aegis of [Central Pollution Control Board](/wiki/Central_Pollution_Control_Board "Central Pollution Control Board") (CPCB), and is headquartered in the city.[^249][^250] As of 2022, Bengaluru produced around 6000 [metric tonnes](/wiki/Metric_tonnes "Metric tonnes") of [solid waste](/wiki/Waste "Waste") per day.[^251] The wastes are segregated, compacted, and transported to any of the three garbage processing plants in Bingipura, [Mavallipura](/wiki/Mavallipura "Mavallipura"), or [Kudlu](/wiki/Kudlu "Kudlu").[^252] As per a 2024 study, the three garbage processing plants were found to be violating environmental regulations, and emitted high levels of [particulate matter](/wiki/Particulate_matter "Particulate matter"), causing damage to the local environment and increasing the pollution levels of the city.[^253] As of 2024, the corporation operated seven wet waste processing plants, 13 bio [methane](/wiki/Methane "Methane") generation plants, and a land fill.[^254] The corporation earlier operated three more landfill sites at [Mavallipura](/wiki/Mavallipura "Mavallipura"), [Mandur](/wiki/Mandur "Mandur"), and [Doddaballapura](/wiki/Doddaballapura "Doddaballapura"), which were closed after complaints from local residents, and reports of diseases due to unsanitary conditions.[^255] In 2024, the government identified four new locations for the construction of new landfill sites.[^256] As part of the waste management guidelines, the government of Karnataka has authorised specific companies to manage [biomedical](/wiki/Biomedical_waste "Biomedical waste") and [e-wastes](/wiki/E-waste "E-waste") in the city.[^257] However, a report in October 2024 indicated that some of these companies were not disposing of the wastes in the prescribed manner, and are involved in re-selling.[^258] 

The city has considerable pollution due to vehicle and industrial exhausts, and unscientific waste disposal.[^259][^260] The pollution level varies across localities, with higher concentrations of [particulate matter](/wiki/Particulate_matter "Particulate matter") reported in industrial and high traffic zones. A [random sampling](/wiki/Random_sample "Random sample") of the [air quality index](/wiki/Air_quality_index "Air quality index") (AQI) of twenty stations within the city suggested heavy to severe air pollution around areas of high traffic.[^261] While the average air quality was at acceptable levels, the [PM 2.5](/wiki/PM_2.5 "PM 2.5") levels exceeded the 60 μg/m3 threshold set by the CPCB in certain areas.[^262] A evaluation of Bengaluru's physical, biological and socioeconomic parameters indicated that the city's air quality and [noise pollution](/wiki/Noise_pollution "Noise pollution") were poor.[^263] 

### Power

In 1905, Bengaluru was among the first cities to have electric power.[^264] The city was powered by [hydro power](/wiki/Hydro_power "Hydro power") generated by the [hydroelectric](/wiki/Hydroelectric "Hydroelectric") plant in [Shivanasamudra](/wiki/Shivanasamudra "Shivanasamudra").[^51] Electricity in the city is regulated through the [Bangalore Electricity Supply Company](/wiki/Bangalore_Electricity_Supply_Company "Bangalore Electricity Supply Company") (BESCOM).[^265] The power consumption has steadily increased over the last decade and in 2022–23, the city had a peak demand of 3,632 [MW](/wiki/Megawatt "Megawatt").[^266][^267] As of March 2024, the city had a daily power requirement of about 157 million [kWh](/wiki/KWh "KWh"), and consumed nearly 40% of the power in the state.[^268] The city draws power from the state grid, which receives power from a mixture of [fossil fuels](/wiki/Fossil_fuels "Fossil fuels") and [renewable](/wiki/Renewable_power "Renewable power") sources.[^269] In 2024, BESCOM initiated the process of moving overhead lines to underground in the city.[^270] 

### Health and sanitation

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Victoria_Hospital-_circa_March_2005.jpg/250px-Victoria_Hospital-_circa_March_2005.jpg)](/wiki/File:Victoria_Hospital-_circa_March_2005.jpg)

[Victoria Hospital](/wiki/Victoria_Hospital_\(Bangalore_Medical_College\) "Victoria Hospital (Bangalore Medical College)") was opened in 1900

In the early 19th century, healthcare services were provided by local physicians. In 1834, English doctors were appointed, to take care of [vaccination](/wiki/Vaccination "Vaccination"), and control the spread of [epidemics](/wiki/Epidemics "Epidemics"). The first public clinic was established in Bangalore Fort in 1835, and a small hospital was added in 1839 in the Pete area. In 1846, a large hospital was opened, with a [leper colony](/wiki/Leper_colony "Leper colony") added in 1845, and a [mental hospital](/wiki/Mental_hospital "Mental hospital") in 1850.[^271][^272] The [Victoria Hospital](/wiki/Victoria_Hospital_\(Bangalore_Medical_College\) "Victoria Hospital (Bangalore Medical College)") was inaugurated in 1900.[^49] As of 2024, the Bengaluru corporation managed one major general hospital, six referral hospitals, 26 maternity homes, and 230 outpatient clinics.[^273][^274] There are many private clinics, and tertiary care hospitals in the city.[^275] The city has been growing as a centre of [medical tourism](/wiki/Medical_tourism "Medical tourism") due to the availability of more than 50 tertiary care hospitals.[^276] Vaccination such as [polio vaccine](/wiki/Polio_vaccine "Polio vaccine") is administered by the corporation on behalf of the government.[^277] 

[Sanitation](/wiki/Sanitation "Sanitation") facilities are provided by the Bangalore Water Supply and Sewerage Board.[^241] The underground drainage and sewerage disposal system was introduced in 1922. As of 2024, about 1,400 million liters of waste water is generated daily, which flows through a network of nearly 8,387 km (5,211 mi) of sewage pipes to any of the 33 sewage treatment plants.[^244] Encroachment, and damages to the sewerage system, has resulted in wastewater entering the lakes, and polluting the water sources.[^244][^278] As of 2024, the corporation operated 401 [public toilets](/wiki/Public_toilet "Public toilet") and 17 community toilets across the city.[^254] 

### Communication

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/General_Post_Office_5-31-2008_4-45-37_PM.JPG/250px-General_Post_Office_5-31-2008_4-45-37_PM.JPG)](/wiki/File:General_Post_Office_5-31-2008_4-45-37_PM.JPG)

Bengaluru General Post Office was established in 1800

The first post office in the city was established in 1800.[^279] Postal services are provided by the government owned [India Post](/wiki/India_Post "India Post"), which operated 247 post offices across four zones in 2024.[^280][^281] In 1853, [telegraph](/wiki/Telegraph "Telegraph") was introduced for long-distance communication and about 538 km (334 mi) of telegraph lines existed in the city by 1856.[^271] [Telephone](/wiki/Telephone "Telephone") services were introduced in 1928.[^264] In the early 1990s, [STPI](/wiki/STPI "STPI") provided wired [internet services](/wiki/Internet_service_provider "Internet service provider") for offices, and [VSNL](/wiki/VSNL "VSNL") started providing [dial up](/wiki/Dial_up "Dial up") connections for individual homes in the city.[^282][^283] Bengaluru has a high internet usage and is amongst the top cities in India in terms of internet penetration.[^284] 

Bengaluru was the first city in India to have access to [fourth generation](/wiki/4G "4G") [cellular](/wiki/Cellular_communication_networks "Cellular communication networks") services.[^285] As of 2023, four mobile phone service companies operate [GSM](/wiki/GSM "GSM") networks including [Bharti Airtel](/wiki/Bharti_Airtel "Bharti Airtel"), [BSNL](/wiki/BSNL "BSNL"), [Vodafone Idea](/wiki/Vodafone_Idea "Vodafone Idea") and [Reliance Jio](/wiki/Reliance_Jio "Reliance Jio") offered fourth and [fifth generation](/wiki/5G "5G") mobile services. Wired broadband services are offered by five major operators and smaller local operators.[^286] Namma Wifi is a free [municipal wireless network](/wiki/Municipal_wireless_network "Municipal wireless network") launched on 24 January 2014 by the Government of Karnataka, and is available in select areas in the city.[^287] 

### Media

The first [printing press](/wiki/Printing_press "Printing press") in Bengaluru was established in 1840  by the [Wesleyan](/wiki/Wesleyan "Wesleyan") Christian Mission.[^288][^289] Around 1860, the English newspaper *Bangalore Herald* and Kannada newspaper *Mysore Vrittanta Bodhini* started circulation in Bengaluru.[^271][^264] P. R. Ramayya established the Bangalore Press in 1927 and launched the Kannada newspaper *Tayi Nadu* and English newspaper *Daily News* later.[^290] Bengaluru has several newspapers and magazines published in various languages including Kannada, English, Urdu, and Tamil.[^291] As of 2022, the major dailies with a circulation of more than 100,000 copies per day include *[The Times of India](/wiki/The_Times_of_India "The Times of India")*, *[Vijaya Karnataka](/wiki/Vijaya_Karnataka "Vijaya Karnataka")*, *[Prajavani](/wiki/Prajavani "Prajavani")*, and *[Vijayavani](/wiki/Vijayavani "Vijayavani")*.[^292] Several local newspapers, and periodicals also bring out editions from the city.[^293] Local online news sites like [Explocity](/wiki/Explocity "Explocity") provide local news updates.[^294] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Aerial_view_of_a_TV_Tower_in_Bangalore_%282%29.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_a_TV_Tower_in_Bangalore_%282%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_a_TV_Tower_in_Bangalore_\(2\).jpg)

The 140 m (460 ft) high television tower, which was commissioned in 1985

[All India Radio](/wiki/All_India_Radio "All India Radio") started [AM](/wiki/Amplitude_modulation "Amplitude modulation") broadcasting from its Bengaluru station on 2 November 1955.[^295] In 2001, [Radio City](/wiki/Radio_City_\(Indian_radio_station\) "Radio City (Indian radio station)") became the first private [FM](/wiki/Frequency_modulation "Frequency modulation") radio channel in the city.[^296] As of 2020, major FM radio stations included [BIG FM](/wiki/BIG_FM_92.7 "BIG FM 92.7"), [Radio Mirchi](/wiki/Radio_Mirchi "Radio Mirchi"), Radio City, and [Red FM](/wiki/Red_FM_\(India\) "Red FM (India)").[^297][^298] The Bangalore Amateur Radio Club, an [amateur radio](/wiki/Amateur_radio "Amateur radio") club was established in 1959.[^299][^300] 

The government run [Doordarshan](/wiki/Doordarshan "Doordarshan") broadcasts terrestrial and [satellite television](/wiki/Satellite_television "Satellite television") channels from its Bengaluru centre set up on 1 November 1981. A production centre was established in the Doordarshan's Bengaluru office in 1983, thereby allowing the introduction of a news programme in Kannada on 19 November 1983.[^301] A 140 m (460 ft) high television tower was commissioned on 1 March 1985 for the broadcast of television programmes.[^302] Doordarshan launched *[DD Chandana](/wiki/DD_Chandana "DD Chandana")*, a Kannada satellite channel, on 15 August 1990.[^301][^303] In September 1991, [Star TV](/wiki/STAR_TV_\(Asia\) "STAR TV (Asia)") was the first private satellite channel to be launched in the city.[^304] Since the late 2000s, [Direct To Home](/wiki/Direct_To_Home "Direct To Home") (DTH) services became available in Bengaluru.[^305] 

### Fire and rescue

Fire services are handled by the [Karnataka Fire and Emergency Services](/wiki/Karnataka_Fire_and_Emergency_Services "Karnataka Fire and Emergency Services"), which operates 50 fire stations, five fire protection squads, and three special units.[^306] 

## Transport

### Air

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bengaluru-airport.jpg/250px-Bengaluru-airport.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bengaluru-airport.jpg)

[Kempegowda International Airport](/wiki/Kempegowda_International_Airport "Kempegowda International Airport") at [Devanahalli](/wiki/Devanahalli "Devanahalli")

During [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), [Walchand Hirachand](/wiki/Walchand_Hirachand "Walchand Hirachand") sought to build and repair planes in India, and partnered with American businessman [William Pawley](/wiki/William_Pawley "William Pawley") to set up an airfield in Bengaluru. The [HAL Airport](/wiki/HAL_Airport "HAL Airport") began operations in 1941 as a part of [Hindustan Aircraft Limited](/wiki/Hindustan_Aeronautics_Limited "Hindustan Aeronautics Limited").[^307][^308] The HAL airport was the major airport of the city till 2008, when the new [Bengaluru International Airport](/wiki/Bengaluru_International_Airport "Bengaluru International Airport") came into existence.[^309][^310][^311] The Kempegowda International Airport, located at [Devanahalli](/wiki/Devanahalli "Devanahalli"), about 31 km (19 mi) from the city, started operations on 24 May 2008.[^312] It is the [third-busiest](/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_in_India "List of busiest airports in India") airport in India in terms of passenger traffic.[^313][^314] Air-conditioned buses operated by [Bengaluru Metropolitan Transport Corporation](/wiki/Bengaluru_Metropolitan_Transport_Corporation "Bengaluru Metropolitan Transport Corporation") connect the airport with the city.[^315] 

The [Training Command](/wiki/Training_Command_\(India\) "Training Command (India)") of the [Indian Air Force](/wiki/Indian_Air_Force "Indian Air Force") is headquartered in Bengaluru.[^316] The Air Force operates an air base at [Yelahanka](/wiki/Yelahanka_Air_Force_Station "Yelahanka Air Force Station").[^317] The city hosts [Aero India](/wiki/Aero_India "Aero India"), a biennial air show at the Yelahanka air force station.[^318][^319] 

### Rail

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/SMVT_Bengaluru.jpg/250px-SMVT_Bengaluru.jpg)](/wiki/File:SMVT_Bengaluru.jpg)

[Sir M. Visvesvaraya Terminal](/wiki/Sir_M._Visvesvaraya_Terminal "Sir M. Visvesvaraya Terminal") railway station at [Baiyappanahalli](/wiki/Baiyappanahalli "Baiyappanahalli")

The first railway line opened for traffic between [Bengaluru Cantonment](/wiki/Bengaluru_Cantonment_railway_station "Bengaluru Cantonment railway station") and [Jolarpettai](/wiki/Jolarpettai_Junction_railway_station "Jolarpettai Junction railway station") on 1 August 1864.[^320][^321] The [Madras-Bangalore Mail](/wiki/Bangalore_Chennai_Mail "Bangalore Chennai Mail") was launched later the same year. Further railway connectivity to [Renigunta](/wiki/Renigunta_Junction_railway_station "Renigunta Junction railway station") was established in 1862, and to [Raichur](/wiki/Raichur_Junction_railway_station "Raichur Junction railway station") in 1871. The [Yeshwantapur station](/wiki/Yesvantpur_Junction_railway_station "Yesvantpur Junction railway station") was established in 1892, when a metre-gauge railway line was established to [Doddaballapur](/wiki/Doddaballapur "Doddaballapur"). The city was part of the [Mysore State Railway](/wiki/Mysore_State_Railway "Mysore State Railway"), which became part of the [Southern Railway zone](/wiki/Southern_Railway_zone "Southern Railway zone") of the [Indian Railways](/wiki/Indian_Railways "Indian Railways") in April 1951. The [Bangalore railway division](/wiki/Bangalore_railway_division "Bangalore railway division") was established in 1971.[^320] The city became part of the [South Western Railway zone](/wiki/South_Western_Railway_zone "South Western Railway zone") was formed with headquarters in [Hubballi](/wiki/Shree_Siddharoodha_Swamiji_Hubballi_Junction_railway_station "Shree Siddharoodha Swamiji Hubballi Junction railway station") in 2003.[^322] There are 18 railway stations in the city managed by the Indian Railways, and the major railway stations include [Bengaluru City](/wiki/Bengaluru_City_railway_station "Bengaluru City railway station"), Yesvantpur, Cantonment, [Krishnarajapuram](/wiki/Krishnarajapuram_railway_station "Krishnarajapuram railway station") and [Baiyappanahalli](/wiki/Sir_M._Visvesvaraya_Terminal "Sir M. Visvesvaraya Terminal").[^216][^323][^324] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Namma_Metro_Trains_of_Bangalore.jpg/250px-Namma_Metro_Trains_of_Bangalore.jpg)](/wiki/File:Namma_Metro_Trains_of_Bangalore.jpg)

[Namma Metro](/wiki/Namma_Metro "Namma Metro") serves the city.

[Namma Metro](/wiki/Namma_Metro "Namma Metro") is a [rapid transit](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") rail system in the city that was opened in 2011, and was the first operational metro in [South India](/wiki/South_India "South India").[^325][^326] As of August 2025, the metro system consists of three operational lines—the Purple, Green, and Yellow Lines—stretching a total of 96.1 km (59.7 mi), making it the second-longest operational metro network in India.[^327] The most recent addition was the Yellow Line, which became fully operational in August 2025, connecting RV Road with Bommasandra.[^328] Five more lines are under construction as a part of expansion.[^329][^330] As of 2026, Bengaluru does not have a [suburban railway network](/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail"). The [Bengaluru Suburban Railway](/wiki/Bengaluru_Suburban_Railway "Bengaluru Suburban Railway") is under construction and the first line is expected to be operational by 2030, though it was originally planned to be completed by October 2026.[^331][^332] 

### Road

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Puttenahalli-Underpass-ORR-JPNagar.jpg/250px-Puttenahalli-Underpass-ORR-JPNagar.jpg)](/wiki/File:Puttenahalli-Underpass-ORR-JPNagar.jpg)

[Outer Ring Road](/wiki/Outer_Ring_Road,_Bengaluru "Outer Ring Road, Bengaluru"), one of the peripheral ring roads in the city

Bengaluru has an extensive road network with about 14,000 km (8,700 mi) of roads as of 2024.[^333] The 10 km (6.2 mi) long [Inner Ring Road](/wiki/Inner_Ring_Road,_Bengaluru "Inner Ring Road, Bengaluru") connects [Koramangala](/wiki/Koramangala "Koramangala") with [Indira Nagar](/wiki/Indiranagar,_Bangalore "Indiranagar, Bangalore").[^334] The [Outer Ring Road](/wiki/Outer_Ring_Road,_Bengaluru "Outer Ring Road, Bengaluru") is a 60 km (37 mi) long peripheral road, developed between 1996 and 2002.[^335] The [Peripheral Ring Road](/wiki/Peripheral_Ring_Road "Peripheral Ring Road") is a proposed 74 km (46 mi) semi-circular road, connecting major arterial roads.[^336] The [M G Road](/wiki/M_G_Road,_Bengaluru "M G Road, Bengaluru") is the major arterial road in the [central business district](/wiki/Bangalore_central_business_district "Bangalore central business district").[^337][^338] Bengaluru is part of the [Golden Quadrilateral](/wiki/Golden_Quadrilateral "Golden Quadrilateral") highway network, and lies on the Chennai–Mumbai line.[^339] The [National Highways](/wiki/List_of_National_Highways_in_India "List of National Highways in India") that connect to the city include: [NH-44](/wiki/National_Highway_44_\(India\) "National Highway 44 (India)"), [NH-48](/wiki/National_Highway_48_\(India\) "National Highway 48 (India)"), [NH-275](/wiki/National_Highway_275_\(India\) "National Highway 275 (India)"), [NH-75](/wiki/National_Highway_75_\(India\) "National Highway 75 (India)"), [NH-648](/wiki/National_Highway_648_\(India\) "National Highway 648 (India)"), and [NH-948](/wiki/National_Highway_948_\(India\) "National Highway 948 (India)").[^340][^341] The [Bengaluru–Mysuru Expressway](/wiki/National_Highway_275_\(India\)#Bengaluru-Mysuru_section "National Highway 275 (India)"), operational since March 2023, connects the city with Mysuru.[^342] The [Bengaluru–Chennai Expressway](/wiki/Bengaluru%E2%80%93Chennai_Expressway "Bengaluru–Chennai Expressway") is under construction since August 2019.[^343][^344] Two other expressways—[Pune–Bengaluru Expressway](/wiki/Pune%E2%80%93Bengaluru_Expressway "Pune–Bengaluru Expressway") and [Nagpur–Hyderabad–Bengaluru Expressway](/wiki/Nagpur%E2%80%93Hyderabad%E2%80%93Bengaluru_Expressway "Nagpur–Hyderabad–Bengaluru Expressway")—have been proposed.[^345][^346] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BMTC_Volvo.jpg/250px-BMTC_Volvo.jpg)](/wiki/File:BMTC_Volvo.jpg)

Air-conditioned buses were introduced by the [BMTC](/wiki/Bengaluru_Metropolitan_Transport_Corporation "Bengaluru Metropolitan Transport Corporation") in 2005

Intra-city [bus services](/wiki/Public_transport "Public transport") is handled by the [Bengaluru Metropolitan Transport Corporation](/wiki/Bengaluru_Metropolitan_Transport_Corporation "Bengaluru Metropolitan Transport Corporation") (BMTC), which was established in 1997.[^347] As of 2024, BMTC operates 57,667 daily trips on 5,766 routes with a fleet of 6,340 buses. There are 48 bus stations, and 50 depots for intra-city bus services.[^348] BMTC introduced air-conditioned buses in 2005, which operate on major routes and as shuttle services from various parts of the city to airport.[^349] It also operates a fleet of more than 1,100 electric vehicles.[^348] Apart from single journey tickets, BMTC issues various passes for frequent users.[^350] Inter-city bus transport is handled by the [Karnataka State Road Transport Corporation](/wiki/Karnataka_State_Road_Transport_Corporation "Karnataka State Road Transport Corporation") (KSRTC), owned by the Government of Karnataka. KSRTC operates various classes of services connecting other major cities in Karnataka, and other neighboring states.[^351] The major bus stations in the city include [Kempegowda Bus Station](/wiki/Kempegowda_Bus_Station "Kempegowda Bus Station"), [Shantinagar Bus Station](/wiki/Shantinagar_Bus_Station "Shantinagar Bus Station"), and [Mysuru Road Bus Station](/wiki/Mysuru_Road_Bus_Station "Mysuru Road Bus Station").[^352][^353] The other means of road transport in the city include vans, [auto rickshaws](/wiki/Auto_rickshaw "Auto rickshaw"), on-call metered taxis and tourist taxis.[^354][^355] 

Motor vehicles were introduced in Bengaluru in 1903.[^356] As of March 2022, an average of 1,530 vehicles were registered daily in [Regional Transport Offices](/wiki/Regional_Transport_Office "Regional Transport Office") (RTOs) in the city.[^357][^358] As of 2023, the city had nearly ten million vehicles including 7.5 million two-wheelers.[^359] The rapid growth of vehicles and unplanned nature of growth has created several administrative problems relating to [traffic congestion](/wiki/Traffic_congestion "Traffic congestion") and infrastructure, resulting in massive traffic [gridlocks](/wiki/Gridlock "Gridlock"). The flyovers and one-way traffic systems introduced to address the concerns, were only moderately successful.[^360] The city also has considerable air pollution due to vehicle exhaust, and a 2016 study found that over 36% of diesel vehicles operating in the city exceeded the standard limit for emissions.[^259][^361] 

## Education

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bangalore_Institution_%28LMS%2C_1869%2C_p.55%29.jpg/250px-Bangalore_Institution_%28LMS%2C_1869%2C_p.55%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bangalore_Institution_\(LMS,_1869,_p.55\).jpg)

An English school established by London mission in 1869

Bengaluru is a major educational hub and home to some of the premium educational institutions in the country.[^362] The city has a 90.33% literacy rate and ranks second among the major Indian metropolitan city centres.[^363] As per the [2011 national census](/wiki/2011_Census_of_India "2011 Census of India"), Bengaluru urban had a literacy rate of around 87.7%.[^364][^365] Until the early 19th century, education in Bengaluru was mainly run by religious leaders and restricted to students of that religion.[^366] In 1841, two native language schools were established by a London mission, and in 1842, [Mummadi Krishnaraja Wodeyar](/wiki/Mummadi_Krishnaraja_Wodeyar "Mummadi Krishnaraja Wodeyar") established the first [English School](/wiki/United_Mission_School "United Mission School") under the Wesleyan mission, which expanded to five schools by 1954. In 1857, a public education department was established, and the education was formulated as per the Indian educational policy at the time.[^271][^264] The [Bangalore Military School](/wiki/Bangalore_Military_School "Bangalore Military School") was established in 1945.[^367] 

Bengaluru has a mix of public and private schools with the public school system managed by the school education department of Government of Karnataka.[^368][^369] Public schools run by the Bengaluru Corporation are all affiliated with the Karnataka Board of Secondary Education, while private schools may be affiliated with either of Karnataka Board of Secondary Education, [Central Board of Secondary Education](/wiki/Central_Board_of_Secondary_Education "Central Board of Secondary Education") (CBSE), [Council for the Indian School Certificate Examinations](/wiki/Council_for_the_Indian_School_Certificate_Examinations "Council for the Indian School Certificate Examinations") (ICSE) or [National Institute of Open Schooling](/wiki/National_Institute_of_Open_Schooling "National Institute of Open Schooling") (NIOS).[^370] As of 2024, there are 142 public schools run by the Bengaluru Corporation.[^371] The city also has a significant number of [international schools](/wiki/International_schools "International schools") due to cater to expats and people employed in the technology sector.[^372] School education starts with two years of Kindergarten from age three onwards and then follows the Indian [10+2 plan](/wiki/Education_in_India "Education in India"), ten years of school and two years of [pre-university course](/wiki/Pre-university_course "Pre-university course") or [higher secondary](/wiki/Higher_secondary "Higher secondary") education. After completing their secondary education, students either attend a [pre-university course](/wiki/Pre-university_course "Pre-university course") or continue an equivalent high school course in one of three streams – [arts](/wiki/Liberal_arts "Liberal arts"), [commerce](/wiki/Commerce "Commerce") or [science](/wiki/Science "Science") – in various combinations.[^373] Alternatively, students can enrol in diploma courses and upon completing the required coursework, students enroll in general or professional degrees in universities through lateral entry.[^374][^375] 

The oldest institution of higher learning in the city, the [Central College](/wiki/Central_College,_Bangalore "Central College, Bangalore"), was established as a high school affiliated to [Madras University](/wiki/Madras_University "Madras University") in 1858.[^271][^376] The [Indian Institute of Science](/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Science "Indian Institute of Science") was established in 1909.[^56][^264] The [Government Engineering College](/wiki/University_of_Visvesvaraya_College_of_Engineering "University of Visvesvaraya College of Engineering") was established as an engineering school in 1913 by [M. Visvesvaraya](/wiki/M._Visvesvaraya "M. Visvesvaraya"), and was became the first engineering college in the region in 1917, affiliated to [Mysore University](/wiki/Mysore_University "Mysore University").[^377] As of 2016, the city had six [public universities](/wiki/Public_universities "Public universities"), four [deemed universities](/wiki/Deemed_universities "Deemed universities"), eight [private universities](/wiki/Private_universities "Private universities"), 26 [medical and dental colleges](/wiki/Medical_college "Medical college"), 84 [engineering colleges](/wiki/Engineering_college "Engineering college"), 67 [polytechnics](/wiki/Institute_of_technology "Institute of technology"), and 64 other institutes of higher learning.[^216] The [Bangalore University](/wiki/Bangalore_University "Bangalore University") was established in 1964, and had more than 600 affiliated colleges, before being trifurcated into [Bengaluru City University](/wiki/Bengaluru_City_University "Bengaluru City University") and [Bengaluru North University](/wiki/Bengaluru_North_University "Bengaluru North University") in 2017.[^378][^379][^380] [IIM Bangalore](/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Bangalore "Indian Institute of Management Bangalore") was established as the third [Indian Institute of Management](/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management "Indian Institute of Management") in 1972.[^381] The [National Institute of Mental Health and Neurosciences](/wiki/National_Institute_of_Mental_Health_and_Neurosciences "National Institute of Mental Health and Neurosciences") was established after the amalgamation of the All India Institute of Mental Health and hospital in 1974.[^382] The [National Law School of India University](/wiki/National_Law_School_of_India_University "National Law School of India University") was the first Indian law university to be established in 1986.[^383] Other prominent research institutes in Bengaluru include [Jawaharlal Nehru Centre for Advanced Scientific Research](/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Centre_for_Advanced_Scientific_Research "Jawaharlal Nehru Centre for Advanced Scientific Research"), [National Centre for Biological Sciences](/wiki/National_Centre_for_Biological_Sciences "National Centre for Biological Sciences"), and [National Institute of Advanced Studies](/wiki/National_Institute_of_Advanced_Studies "National Institute of Advanced Studies").[^384] There are 205 public libraries maintained by the department of public libraries. The libraries are divided across the five zones of the city, with a larger Central Public Library located in each of the zones.[^385] 

## Parks and recreation

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Stage-1-cubbon_park-bangalore-India.jpg/250px-Stage-1-cubbon_park-bangalore-India.jpg)](/wiki/File:Stage-1-cubbon_park-bangalore-India.jpg)

[Cubbon Park](/wiki/Cubbon_Park "Cubbon Park"), established in 1870, is a large park in the centre of the city

Bengaluru is known as the "Garden City of India" because of its greenery.[^386][^387] In May 2012, [Lonely Planet](/wiki/Lonely_Planet "Lonely Planet") listed the city as one of the world's top ten cities to visit.[^388] As of 2024, Bengaluru has 1,288 public parks maintained by the corporation.[^389] The [Lal Bagh](/wiki/Lal_Bagh "Lal Bagh") was established in the 1760s, and was later expanded into a 97 ha (240 acres) botanical garden in the 19th century. It incorporates a hillock made of [gneiss](/wiki/Gneiss "Gneiss"), formed billions of years ago, and is a declared national geological monument. The garden has a watch tower built in the 16th century by Kempe Gowda, a glass house built in 1889 on the model of [The Crystal Palace](/wiki/The_Crystal_Palace "The Crystal Palace") in London, old [hero stones](/wiki/Hero_stone "Hero stone"), and houses many exotic species of plants.[^390] A [biannual](/wiki/Biannual "Biannual") flowershow is held at the gardens during the weeks of India's [Republic Day](/wiki/Republic_Day_\(India\) "Republic Day (India)") and [Independence Day](/wiki/Independence_Day_\(India\) "Independence Day (India)").[^391][^392] 

The [Cubbon Park](/wiki/Cubbon_Park "Cubbon Park") is a large park spanning 120 ha (300 acres) in the heart of the city, and was established in 1870. It hosts the [Bangalore Aquarium](/wiki/Bangalore_Aquarium "Bangalore Aquarium"), and the [Bangalore central library](/wiki/Bangalore_central_library "Bangalore central library").[^393][^394] [Bannerghatta National Park](/wiki/Bannerghatta_National_Park "Bannerghatta National Park") is a 260.51 km2 (100.58 sq mi) [national park and protected area](/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_India "List of protected areas of India"), located south of the city.[^395] The old central prison was decommissioned in 2000 and was redeveloped in to [Freedom Park](/wiki/Freedom_Park,_Bangalore "Freedom Park, Bangalore").[^396] 

Elgin Talkies, built in 1896, was the first theatre in Bengaluru.[^397] In the later half of the 20th century, the city had 149 single screens, most of them situated along the Kempegowda Road near the [Kempegowda Bus Station](/wiki/Kempegowda_Bus_Station "Kempegowda Bus Station").[^398] In the 21st century, large multiplexes with multiple screens began replacing the single screen theatres, and the city is now home to a large number of multiplexes.[^399][^400] Stage plays and dramas of different genres and languages are enacted in theatres across the city.[^401][^402] 

## Sports

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Chinnaswamy_Stadium.jpg/250px-Chinnaswamy_Stadium.jpg)](/wiki/File:Chinnaswamy_Stadium.jpg)

[Chinnaswamy Stadium](/wiki/Chinnaswamy_Stadium "Chinnaswamy Stadium") in 2017

[Cricket](/wiki/Cricket "Cricket") is the most popular sport in the city and the parks in the city serve as venues for impromptu games.[^403][^404][^405] [M. Chinnaswamy Stadium](/wiki/M._Chinnaswamy_Stadium "M. Chinnaswamy Stadium"), established in 1969, is a major [international cricketing venue](/wiki/List_of_international_cricket_grounds_in_India "List of international cricket grounds in India"), and has hosted matches during multiple [ICC Cricket World Cups](/wiki/ICC_Cricket_World_Cup "ICC Cricket World Cup").[^406] The [Karnataka State Cricket Association](/wiki/Karnataka_State_Cricket_Association "Karnataka State Cricket Association"), located in the stadium premises, is responsible for managing organised cricket in the state.[^407] The [National Cricket Academy](/wiki/National_Cricket_Academy "National Cricket Academy"), operated by the [Board of Control for Cricket in India](/wiki/Board_of_Control_for_Cricket_in_India "Board of Control for Cricket in India"), is based out of the city.[^408] The city is home to the [Indian Premier League](/wiki/Indian_Premier_League "Indian Premier League") (IPL) franchise [Royal Challengers Bengaluru](/wiki/Royal_Challengers_Bengaluru "Royal Challengers Bengaluru").[^409] Notable international cricketers born in the city include [Erapalli Prasanna](/wiki/Erapalli_Prasanna "Erapalli Prasanna"),[^410] [Roger Binny](/wiki/Roger_Binny "Roger Binny"),[^411] [Anil Kumble](/wiki/Anil_Kumble "Anil Kumble"),[^412] [Venkatesh Prasad](/wiki/Venkatesh_Prasad "Venkatesh Prasad"),[^413] [Lokesh Rahul](/wiki/Lokesh_Rahul "Lokesh Rahul"),[^414] [Mayank Agarwal](/wiki/Mayank_Agarwal "Mayank Agarwal"),[^415] and [Stuart Binny](/wiki/Stuart_Binny "Stuart Binny").[^416] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Sree_Kanteerava_Stadium.jpg/250px-Sree_Kanteerava_Stadium.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sree_Kanteerava_Stadium.jpg)

[Sree Kanteerava Stadium](/wiki/Sree_Kanteerava_Stadium "Sree Kanteerava Stadium")

[Sree Kanteerava Stadium](/wiki/Sree_Kanteerava_Stadium "Sree Kanteerava Stadium") is a multi-purpose venue which hosts [football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") and [athletics](/wiki/Sport_of_athletics "Sport of athletics").[^417][^418] Association football also has a significant following in the city, and [Bangalore Football Stadium](/wiki/Bangalore_Football_Stadium "Bangalore Football Stadium") hosts football matches along with the Kanteerva stadium in the city.[^418][^419] The city is home to football clubs [Bengaluru FC](/wiki/Bengaluru_FC "Bengaluru FC"),[^420] [FC Bengaluru United](/wiki/FC_Bengaluru_United "FC Bengaluru United"),[^421] [Ozone FC](/wiki/Ozone_FC "Ozone FC"),[^422] [South United FC](/wiki/South_United_FC "South United FC"),[^423] and [SC Bengaluru](/wiki/SC_Bengaluru "SC Bengaluru").[^424] Prominent international footballers from the city include [Sattar Basheer](/wiki/Sattar_Basheer "Sattar Basheer"), and [Arumainayagam](/wiki/Arumainayagam "Arumainayagam").[^425] The [Kanteerava Indoor Stadium](/wiki/Kanteerava_Indoor_Stadium "Kanteerava Indoor Stadium") and [Koramangala Indoor Stadium](/wiki/Koramangala_Indoor_Stadium "Koramangala Indoor Stadium") are [indoor arenas](/wiki/Indoor_arena "Indoor arena") used to host indoor sports, and other events.[^426][^427] The Kanteerva arena hosted the [South Asian Basketball Championship](/wiki/SABA_Championship "SABA Championship") in [2015](/wiki/2015_SABA_Championship "2015 SABA Championship") and [2016](/wiki/2016_SABA_Championship "2016 SABA Championship").[^428][^429] The city is home to [Bengaluru Beast](/wiki/Bengaluru_Beast "Bengaluru Beast") of the [UBA Pro Basketball League](/wiki/UBA_Pro_Basketball_League "UBA Pro Basketball League"),[^430] and [Bengaluru Bulls](/wiki/Bengaluru_Bulls "Bengaluru Bulls") of the [Pro Kabaddi League](/wiki/Pro_Kabaddi_League "Pro Kabaddi League"), who also play their home matches at the stadium.[^431][^432] 

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BFS_on_a_matchday_May_2023.jpg/250px-BFS_on_a_matchday_May_2023.jpg)](/wiki/File:BFS_on_a_matchday_May_2023.jpg)

[Bangalore Football Stadium](/wiki/Bangalore_Football_Stadium "Bangalore Football Stadium")

Bengaluru hosts the [WTA Indian Open](/wiki/WTA_Indian_Open "WTA Indian Open"), and [Bengaluru Open](/wiki/Bengaluru_Open "Bengaluru Open") [tennis](/wiki/Tennis "Tennis") tournaments annually.[^433][^434] Prominent international sports people from the city include tennis [grand slam](/wiki/Grand_Slam_\(tennis\) "Grand Slam (tennis)") champion [Rohan Bopanna](/wiki/Rohan_Bopanna "Rohan Bopanna"),[^435] former [All England Open](/wiki/All_England_Open "All England Open") [badminton](/wiki/Badminton "Badminton") champion [Prakash Padukone](/wiki/Prakash_Padukone "Prakash Padukone"),[^436] and former national [swimming](/wiki/Swimming "Swimming") champion [Nisha Millet](/wiki/Nisha_Millet "Nisha Millet").[^437] Other notable sportsmen who reside in the city include former [Indian cricket captain](/wiki/List_of_India_national_cricket_captains "List of India national cricket captains") [Rahul Dravid](/wiki/Rahul_Dravid "Rahul Dravid"),[^438] [world snooker champion](/wiki/World_snooker_champion "World snooker champion") [Pankaj Advani](/wiki/Pankaj_Advani_\(billiards_player\) "Pankaj Advani (billiards player)"),[^439] and multiple tennis [grand slam](/wiki/Grand_Slam_\(tennis\) "Grand Slam (tennis)") champion [Mahesh Bhupathi](/wiki/Mahesh_Bhupathi "Mahesh Bhupathi").[^440] The city is home to several recreational and sports clubs such as [Bangalore Club](/wiki/Bangalore_Club "Bangalore Club"), [Bowring Institute](/wiki/Bowring_Institute "Bowring Institute"), Bangalore Golf Club and Bangalore Turf Club.[^441][^442]

## Foreign relations

Bengaluru has consulates of France,[^451] [Germany](/wiki/Consulate_General_of_Germany,_Bangalore "Consulate General of Germany, Bangalore"),[^452] Israel,[^453] and Japan,[^454] and a virtual consulate of the United States.[^455] The city also hosts a British deputy High Commission,[^456] and honorary consulates of Finland,[^457] Ireland,[^458] Maldives,[^459] Peru,[^460] and Switzerland.[^461] Canada has a trade office in the city.[^462] 

Bengaluru has a [sister city](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") relationship with the following cities: 

*   [Minsk, Belarus](/wiki/Minsk,_Belarus "Minsk, Belarus") (1973)[^463]
*   [Cleveland](/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio "Cleveland, Ohio"), United States (1992)[^464]
*   [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco,_California "San Francisco, California"), United States (2008)[^465]
*   [Chengdu](/wiki/Chengdu,_Sichuan "Chengdu, Sichuan"), China (2013)[^466]
